Thesis Reference Regulation of dynamin - mediated membrane fission by the N - BAR protein endophilin HOHENDAHL , Annika Abstract Eukaryotic cells are composed of different compartments with defined biological functions . Transport of molecules from one compartment to another , as well as from and to the plasma membrane , occurs via membrane vesicles . Clathrin - mediated endocytosis is the most studied pathway for the formation of such a vesicle . The GTPase dynamin mediates the final membrane fission step in this process . This thesis describes the experimental work to clarify how a specific class of crescent - shaped proteins called N - BAR proteins regulate dynamin - mediated membrane fission . Endophilin , one of the N - BAR proteins , was taken as an example . The major experimental technique is the nanotube pulling assay , an in - vitro essay using purified proteins . Other chapters of this thesis explore curvature - inducing properties of the clathrin adapter AP180 and the curvature - dependent activity of yeast Vps34 complex I . Additionally , this thesis analyses structural consequences of mutations in dynamin and another N - BAR protein , BIN1 / amphiphysin 2 , which cause the hereditary muscle disease CNM ( centronuclear myopathy ) . HOHENDAHL , Annika . Regulation of dynamin - mediated membrane fission by the N - BAR protein endophilin . Thèse de doctorat : Univ . Genève , 2016 , no . Sc . 5031 URN : urn : nbn : ch : unige - 918330 DOI : 10 . 13097 / archive - ouverte / unige : 91833 Available at : http : / / archive - ouverte . unige . ch / unige : 91833 Disclaimer : layout of this document may differ from the published version . 1 / 1 UNIVERSITÉ DE GENÈVE FACULTÉ DES SCIENCES Section de chimie et biochimie Département de biochimie Professeur Aurélien Roux Regulation of Dynamin - Mediated Membrane Fission by the N - BAR Protein Endophilin THÈSE présentée à la Faculté des sciences de l’Université de Genève pour obtenir le grade de Docteur ès sciences , mention biochimie par Annika HOHENDAHL de Düsseldorf ( Allemagne ) Thèse N ◦ 5031 GENÈVE Atelier de reproduction ReproMail 2016 Résumé La cellule est l’unité de base des organismes vivants . Les cellules eucaryotes contiennent diﬀérents compartiments intracellulaires ayant des propriétés chimiques et des fonctions bi - ologiques bien déﬁnies . Le transport de molécules entre de tels compartiments , ainsi qu’entre un compartiment et la membrane plasmique entourant la cellule , a lieu par l’intermédiaire des vésicules membranaires . L’endocytose médiée par la clathrine est la voie biologique la plus étudiée pour la formation d’une vésicule membranaire . On déﬁnit l’endocytose par la formation d’une vésicule à partir de la membrane plasmique vers l’espace intracellulaire . Les organismes unicellulaires utilisent l’endocytose pour absorber des nutriments depuis l’espace extracellulaire . Chez les eucaryotes multicellulaires , l’endocytose a également pour fonction la régulation du contenu protéique de la membrane plasmique ainsi que la formation de vésicules présynaptiques qui sont ensuite remplies de neurotransmetteurs et libérées dans l’espace intersynaptique suite à l’arrivée d’un potentiel d’action . Dans l’endocytose médiée par la clathrine , la membrane est d’abord courbée en un puits peu profond puis en un bourgeon qui s’accroît sous l’action de la clathrine et de plusieurs autres facteurs . Il y a ensuite constriction du cou du bourgeon et ﬁssion de la membrane grâce à la dynamine , libérant la vésicule de la membrane d’origine . La dynamine forme des spirales autour des cous membranaires et convertit l’énergie d’hydrolyse de guanosine triphosphate ( GTP ) en une activité de torsion qui conduit à la constriction du tube membranaire sous - jacent . La famille des protéines BIN / Amphiphysin / Rvs ( BAR ) , dont le domaine BAR a une forme de croissant , est aussi localisée au niveau du cou du bourgeon à diﬀérents stades de l’endocytose médiée par la clathrine . Un sous - groupe des protéines BAR appelé protéines N - BAR ont une hélice amphipathique N - terminale . De part leur apparition au niveau du cou membranaire juste avant la ﬁssion de la vésicule , de leurs propriétés inductrice de courbure et de leurs interactions avec la dynamine à travers un domaine spéciﬁque , les protéines N - BAR sont des candidates pos - sibles à la régulation de la ﬁssion membranaire . Comme des résultats contradictoires ont été obtenus concernant la nature de cette régulation , le rôle des protéines N - BAR dans la ﬁssion membranaire est toujours incertain . La partie principale de cette thèse décrit le travail expérimental que j’ai mené aﬁn de clari - ﬁer comment les protéines N - BAR régulent la ﬁssion membranaire médiée par la dynamine . L’endophiline , une des protéines N - BAR , a été choisie en tant qu’exemple . Les vitesses et les eﬃcacités de ﬁssion ont été mesurées à l’aide d’un système expérimental dans lequel des pro - téines puriﬁées sont injectées sur un nanotube membranaire étiré à partir d’une vésicule géante ayant une composition lipidique déﬁnie . Mes résultats sont en accord avec un mécanisme par lequel l’endophiline inhibe la ﬁssion membranaire médiée par la dynamine en s’insérant entre les tours de la spirale de dynamine . Dans un autre chapitre , les propriétés inductrices de courbure de l’adaptateur de clathrine iv AP180 sont explorées , utilisant le système expérimental d’extrusion de nanotube . Ces résultats indiquent que la clathrine était nécessaire pour obtenir les propriétés observées d’un mélange de clathrine et d’AP180 . La dernière partie de cette thèse discute les résultats d’expériences en vue de détecter une activité dépendante de la courbure du complexe I de Vps34 de la levure qui est impliqué dans l’autophagie . Un potentiel eﬀet de dépendance à la courbure semble peu manifeste . Ce manuscrit contient par ailleurs une analyse des conséquences structurelles dûes à des mu - tations dans la dynamine et une autre protéine N - BAR , BIN1 / amphiphysine 2 , qui causent la maladie héréditaire musculaire MCN ( myopathie centronucléaire ) dans le cadre d’une revue . Nous proposons un modèle dans lequel les conséquences spéciﬁques aux muscles des mutations dans ces protéines omniprésentes sont dûes aux propriétés d’échaﬀaudage des deux protéines dans le muscle qui sont altérées quand l’équilibre entre les deux protéines est perturbé . Abstract The basic unit of living organisms is the cell . Eukaryotic cells are composed of diﬀerent in - tracellular compartments with deﬁned chemical properties and biological functions . Transport of molecules from one compartment to another , as well as from and to the plasma membrane that surrounds the cell , occurs via membrane vesicles . The most studied biological pathway for the formation of a membrane vesicle is clathrin - mediated endocytosis . Endocytosis denotes the formation of a vesicle from the plasma membrane towards the intracellular space . Unicellular organisms use endocytosis to take up nutrients from the extracellular space . One function of endocytosis in multicellular organisms is also the regulation of the protein content of the plasma membrane and the formation of presynaptic vesicles that are in the following ﬁlled with neurotransmitter and released into the synaptic cleft upon an arriving action potential . In clathrin - mediated endocytosis , the membrane is ﬁrst bent into a shallow pit and later into a growing bud by clathrin and several other factors . The neck of the bud is then constricted and dynamin - mediated membrane ﬁssion releases the vesicle from the donor membrane . Dynamin forms helices around membrane necks and converts the energy from guanosine triphosphate ( GTP ) hydrolysis into a torque that constricts the underlying membrane tube . The crescent - shaped BIN / Amphiphysin / Rvs ( BAR ) proteins also locate to the bud neck at diﬀerent stages of clathrin - mediated endocytosis . One subgroup of the BAR proteins are called N - BAR proteins due to their N - terminal amphipathic helix . Due to their appearance at the neck just before vesicle ﬁssion , their curvature inducing properties and interaction with dynamin via a speciﬁc domain , N - BAR proteins were proposed to regulate membrane ﬁssion . As contradictory results were obtained concerning the nature of the regulation , the role of N - BAR proteins in membrane ﬁssion is still unclear . The main part of this thesis describes the experimental work that I have done to clarify how N - BAR proteins regulate dynamin - mediated membrane ﬁssion . Endophilin , one of the N - BAR proteins , was taken as an example . Fission rates and eﬃciencies were measured using an ex - perimental system in which puriﬁed proteins are injected on a membrane nanotube that was pulled from a giant vesicle of deﬁned lipid composition . My results agree with a mechanism by which endophilin inhibits dynamin - mediated membrane ﬁssion by inserting between dynamin helix turns . In another chapter , curvature - inducing properties of the clathrin adapter AP180 are explored , using the above nanotube pulling assay . These outcomes indicated that clathrin was required for the observed curvature - inducing properties of a mixture of clathrin and AP180 . The last part of this thesis discusses the outcomes of experiments to detect curvature - dependent activity of yeast Vps34 complex I that is involved in autophagy . A potential curvature eﬀect does not seem to be very high . vi Additionally , this manuscript contains an analysis of structural consequences of mutations in dynamin and another N - BAR protein , BIN1 / amphiphysin 2 , which cause the hereditary muscle disease CNM ( centronuclear myopathy ) in the framework of a review . We propose a model in which the muscle - speciﬁc consequences of the mutations in these ubiquitous proteins are due to scaﬀolding properties of both proteins in the muscle which are impaired when the equilibrium between the two proteins is disturbed . Mediated Endocytosis Active intracellular transport of molecules between cellular compartments is an essential process in the cell . It allows to deliver a molecule to a target compartment that is diﬀerent from the compartment in which it had been synthesised or been before . Cells use this system to adapt to their current environment by changing the concentration of speciﬁc receptors on the plasma membrane or to take up speciﬁc nutrients from the extracellular space . Transport is required as well for molecules that are directly bound to the membrane as well as for molecules that are in solution . An example for molecules in solution are neurotransmitters that are speciﬁcally secreted into the synaptic cleft between two neurons in the brain upon an action potential by exocytosis . For intracellular transport , membrane vesicles are the major carrier . A vesicle is generated from the donor membrane compartment , containing the desired molecules , and then transported to the target compartment where it fuses with the target membrane and delivers the soluble content as well as the lipids and membrane - bound molecules to the new compartment . Diﬀerent machineries are involved in the formation of these vesicles , depending on the speciﬁc transport pathway . The most studied endocytic pathway is clathrin - mediated endocytosis ( CME ) . The sequence of events during CME is depicted in Figure 1 . 1 . (cid:49)(cid:86)(cid:74)(cid:71)(cid:84)(cid:2)(cid:69)(cid:67)(cid:84)(cid:73)(cid:81) (cid:67)(cid:70)(cid:67)(cid:82)(cid:86)(cid:81)(cid:84)(cid:85) (cid:37)(cid:81)(cid:80)(cid:80)(cid:71)(cid:69)(cid:70)(cid:71)(cid:80)(cid:80)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2) (cid:38)(cid:91)(cid:80)(cid:67)(cid:79)(cid:75)(cid:80)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2) Figure 2 | The clathrin - coated vesicle cycle . a | The proposed five steps of clathrin - coated vesicle formation . Nucleation : FCH domain only ( FCHO ) proteins bind phosphatidylinositol - 4 , 5 - bisphosphate ( PtdIns ( 4 , 5 ) P 2 ) - rich zones of the plasma membrane and recruit EPS15 – EPS15R ( EGFR pathway substrate 15 – EPS15 - related ) and intersectins to initiate clathrin - coated pit formation by recruiting adaptor protein 2 ( AP2 ) . Cargo selection : AP2 recruits several classes of receptors directly through its μ - subunit and σ - subunit . Cargo - specific adaptors ( for example , stonin , HRB and Numb ) bind to AP2 appendage domains and recruit specific receptors to the AP2 hub . Coat assembly : clathrin triskelia are recruited by the AP2 hub and polymerize in hexagons and pentagons to form the clathrin coat around the nascent pit . Scission : the GTPase dynamin is recruited at the neck of the forming vesicle by BAR domain - containing proteins , where it self - polymerizes and , upon GTP hydrolysis , induces membrane scission . The actin machinery module can be added at this stage for actin polymerization at the neck of the pit , which can aid in vesicle production ( not shown ) . Uncoating : auxilin or cyclin G - associated kinase ( GAK ) recruit the ATPase heat shock cognate 70 ( HSC70 ) to disassemble the clathrin coat and produce an endocytic vesicle containing the cargo molecules . Synaptojanin probably facilitates this by releasing adaptor proteins from the vesicle membrane through its PtdIns lipid phosphatase activity . The components of the clathrin machinery are then freed and become available for another round of clathrin - coated vesicle formation . b | The clathrin network . The protein – protein interactions underlying the different stages of vesicle progression are shown . Major hubs are obvious because of their central location in the network and the large number of interacting molecules . They are essential for pathway progression and are denoted by the central coloured circles . Possible pathways of progression between hubs are shown with thicker lines . c | Effects of depletion of different components of the clathrin machinery . Epithelial cells expressing FCHO2 tagged with red fluorescent protein ( RFP ) , AP2 tagged on the σ 2 subunit with enhanced green fluorescent protein ( σ 2 – EGFP ) and clathrin tagged with blue fluorescent protein ( BFP ) show arrests at each successive stage in clathrin - coated pit formation after perturbation of major hubs . FCHO protein depletion through RNA interference ( RNAi ) inhibits AP2 and clathrin recruitment to the plasma membrane ( and both remain diffuse and cytosolic ) . AP2 RNAi abrogates clathrin recruitment to the plasma membrane but not FCHO2 initial focus formation ( dense red spots ) . Clathrin RNAi blocks maturation during cargo selection , when FCHO2 and AP2 are clustered ( yellow dots , arrows ) . Dynamin inhibition ( by dynasore ) blocks clathrin - coated pits at a stage just before membrane scission ( white dots , arrows ) . AAK , AP2 - associated protein kinase 1 ; ARP2 / 3 , actin - related protein 2 / 3 ; DAB2 , Disabled homologue 2 ; HIP1R , HIP1 - related ; N - WASP , neural Wiskott – Aldrich syndrome protein ; NECAP , adaptin ear - binding coat - associated protein ; SNX9 , sorting nexin 9 . (cid:38)(cid:91)(cid:80)(cid:67)(cid:79)(cid:75)(cid:80)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2) Figure 2 | The clathrin - coated vesicle cycle . a | The proposed five steps of clathrin - coated vesicle formation . Nucleation : FCH domain only ( FCHO ) proteins bind phosphatidylinositol - 4 , 5 - bisphosphate ( PtdIns ( 4 , 5 ) P 2 ) - rich zones of the plasma membrane and recruit EPS15 – EPS15R ( EGFR pathway substrate 15 – EPS15 - related ) and intersectins to initiate clathrin - coated pit formation by recruiting adaptor protein 2 ( AP2 ) . Cargo selection : AP2 recruits several classes of receptors directly through its μ - subunit and σ - subunit . Cargo - specific adaptors ( for example , stonin , HRB and Numb ) bind to AP2 appendage domains and recruit specific receptors to the AP2 hub . Coat assembly : clathrin triskelia are recruited by the AP2 hub and polymerize in hexagons and pentagons to form the clathrin coat around the nascent pit . Scission : the GTPase dynamin is recruited at the neck of the forming vesicle by BAR domain - containing proteins , where it self - polymerizes and , upon GTP hydrolysis , induces membrane scission . The actin machinery module can be added at this stage for actin polymerization at the neck of the pit , which can aid in vesicle production ( not shown ) . Uncoating : auxilin or cyclin G - associated kinase ( GAK ) recruit the ATPase heat shock cognate 70 ( HSC70 ) to disassemble the clathrin coat and produce an endocytic vesicle containing the cargo molecules . Synaptojanin probably facilitates this by releasing adaptor proteins from the vesicle membrane through its PtdIns lipid phosphatase activity . The components of the clathrin machinery are then freed and become available for another round of clathrin - coated vesicle formation . b | The clathrin network . The protein – protein interactions underlying the different stages of vesicle progression are shown . Major hubs are obvious because of their central location in the network and the large number of interacting molecules . They are essential for pathway progression and are denoted by the central coloured circles . Possible pathways of progression between hubs are shown with thicker lines . c | Effects of depletion of different components of the clathrin machinery . Epithelial cells expressing FCHO2 tagged with red fluorescent protein ( RFP ) , AP2 tagged on the σ 2 subunit with enhanced green fluorescent protein ( σ 2 – EGFP ) and clathrin tagged with blue fluorescent protein ( BFP ) show arrests at each successive stage in clathrin - coated pit formation after perturbation of major hubs . FCHO protein depletion through RNA interference ( RNAi ) inhibits AP2 and clathrin recruitment to the plasma membrane ( and both remain diffuse and cytosolic ) . AP2 RNAi abrogates clathrin recruitment to the plasma membrane but not FCHO2 initial focus formation ( dense red spots ) . Clathrin RNAi blocks maturation during cargo selection , when FCHO2 and AP2 are clustered ( yellow dots , arrows ) . Dynamin inhibition ( by dynasore ) blocks clathrin - coated pits at a stage just before membrane scission ( white dots , arrows ) . (cid:49)(cid:86)(cid:74)(cid:71)(cid:84)(cid:2)(cid:69)(cid:67)(cid:84)(cid:73)(cid:81) (cid:67)(cid:70)(cid:67)(cid:82)(cid:86)(cid:81)(cid:84)(cid:85) (cid:37)(cid:81)(cid:80)(cid:80)(cid:71)(cid:69)(cid:70)(cid:71)(cid:80)(cid:80)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2) (cid:38)(cid:91)(cid:80)(cid:67)(cid:79)(cid:75)(cid:80)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2) Figure 2 | The clathrin - coated vesicle cycle . a | The proposed five steps of clathrin - coated vesicle formation . Nucleation : FCH domain only ( FCHO ) proteins bind phosphatidylinositol - 4 , 5 - bisphosphate ( PtdIns ( 4 , 5 ) P 2 ) - rich zones of the plasma membrane and recruit EPS15 – EPS15R ( EGFR pathway substrate 15 – EPS15 - related ) and intersectins to initiate clathrin - coated pit formation by recruiting adaptor protein 2 ( AP2 ) . Cargo selection : AP2 recruits several classes of receptors directly through its μ - subunit and σ - subunit . Cargo - specific adaptors ( for example , stonin , HRB and Numb ) bind to AP2 appendage domains and recruit specific receptors to the AP2 hub . Coat assembly : clathrin triskelia are recruited by the AP2 hub and polymerize in hexagons and pentagons to form the clathrin coat around the nascent pit . Scission : the GTPase dynamin is recruited at the neck of the forming vesicle by BAR domain - containing proteins , where it self - polymerizes and , upon GTP hydrolysis , induces membrane scission . The actin machinery module can be added at this stage for actin polymerization at the neck of the pit , which can aid in vesicle production ( not shown ) . Uncoating : auxilin or cyclin G - associated kinase ( GAK ) recruit the ATPase heat shock cognate 70 ( HSC70 ) to disassemble the clathrin coat and produce an endocytic vesicle containing the cargo molecules . Synaptojanin probably facilitates this by releasing adaptor proteins from the vesicle membrane through its PtdIns lipid phosphatase activity . The components of the clathrin machinery are then freed and become available for another round of clathrin - coated vesicle formation . b | The clathrin network . The protein – protein interactions underlying the different stages of vesicle progression are shown . Major hubs are obvious because of their central location in the network and the large number of interacting molecules . They are essential for pathway progression and are denoted by the central coloured circles . Possible pathways of progression between hubs are shown with thicker lines . c | Effects of depletion of different components of the clathrin machinery . Epithelial cells expressing FCHO2 tagged with red fluorescent protein ( RFP ) , AP2 tagged on the σ 2 subunit with enhanced green fluorescent protein ( σ 2 – EGFP ) and clathrin tagged with blue fluorescent protein ( BFP ) show arrests at each successive stage in clathrin - coated pit formation after perturbation of major hubs . FCHO protein depletion through RNA interference ( RNAi ) inhibits AP2 and clathrin recruitment to the plasma membrane ( and both remain diffuse and cytosolic ) . AP2 RNAi abrogates clathrin recruitment to the plasma membrane but not FCHO2 initial focus formation ( dense red spots ) . Clathrin RNAi blocks maturation during cargo selection , when FCHO2 and AP2 are clustered ( yellow dots , arrows ) . Dynamin inhibition ( by dynasore ) blocks clathrin - coated pits at a stage just before membrane scission ( white dots , arrows ) . AAK , AP2 - associated protein kinase 1 ; ARP2 / 3 , actin - related protein 2 / 3 ; DAB2 , Disabled homologue 2 ; HIP1R , HIP1 - related ; N - WASP , neural Wiskott – Aldrich syndrome protein ; NECAP , adaptin ear - binding coat - associated protein ; SNX9 , sorting nexin 9 . (cid:38)(cid:91)(cid:80)(cid:67)(cid:79)(cid:75)(cid:80)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2) Figure 2 | The clathrin - coated vesicle cycle . a | The proposed five steps of clathrin - coated vesicle formation . Nucleation : FCH domain only ( FCHO ) proteins bind phosphatidylinositol - 4 , 5 - bisphosphate ( PtdIns ( 4 , 5 ) P 2 ) - rich zones of the plasma membrane and recruit EPS15 – EPS15R ( EGFR pathway substrate 15 – EPS15 - related ) and intersectins to initiate clathrin - coated pit formation by recruiting adaptor protein 2 ( AP2 ) . Cargo selection : AP2 recruits several classes of receptors directly through its μ - subunit and σ - subunit . Cargo - specific adaptors ( for example , stonin , HRB and Numb ) bind to AP2 appendage domains and recruit specific receptors to the AP2 hub . Coat assembly : clathrin triskelia are recruited by the AP2 hub and polymerize in hexagons and pentagons to form the clathrin coat around the nascent pit . Scission : the GTPase dynamin is recruited at the neck of the forming vesicle by BAR domain - containing proteins , where it self - polymerizes and , upon GTP hydrolysis , induces membrane scission . The actin machinery module can be added at this stage for actin polymerization at the neck of the pit , which can aid in vesicle production ( not shown ) . Uncoating : auxilin or cyclin G - associated kinase ( GAK ) recruit the ATPase heat shock cognate 70 ( HSC70 ) to disassemble the clathrin coat and produce an endocytic vesicle containing the cargo molecules . Synaptojanin probably facilitates this by releasing adaptor proteins from the vesicle membrane through its PtdIns lipid phosphatase activity . The components of the clathrin machinery are then freed and become available for another round of clathrin - coated vesicle formation . b | The clathrin network . The protein – protein interactions underlying the different stages of vesicle progression are shown . Major hubs are obvious because of their central location in the network and the large number of interacting molecules . They are essential for pathway progression and are denoted by the central coloured circles . Possible pathways of progression between hubs are shown with thicker lines . c | Effects of depletion of different components of the clathrin machinery . Epithelial cells expressing FCHO2 tagged with red fluorescent protein ( RFP ) , AP2 tagged on the σ 2 subunit with enhanced green fluorescent protein ( σ 2 – EGFP ) and clathrin tagged with blue fluorescent protein ( BFP ) show arrests at each successive stage in clathrin - coated pit formation after perturbation of major hubs . FCHO protein depletion through RNA interference ( RNAi ) inhibits AP2 and clathrin recruitment to the plasma membrane ( and both remain diffuse and cytosolic ) . AP2 RNAi abrogates clathrin recruitment to the plasma membrane but not FCHO2 initial focus formation ( dense red spots ) . Clathrin RNAi blocks maturation during cargo selection , when FCHO2 and AP2 are clustered ( yellow dots , arrows ) . Dynamin inhibition ( by dynasore ) blocks clathrin - coated pits at a stage just before membrane scission ( white dots , arrows ) . AAK , AP2 - associated protein kinase 1 ; ARP2 / 3 , actin - related protein 2 / 3 ; DAB2 , Disabled homologue 2 ; HIP1R , HIP1 - related ; N - WASP , neural Wiskott – Aldrich syndrome protein ; NECAP , adaptin ear - binding coat - associated protein ; SNX9 , sorting nexin 9 . (cid:49)(cid:86)(cid:74)(cid:71)(cid:84)(cid:2)(cid:69)(cid:67)(cid:84)(cid:73)(cid:81)(cid:67)(cid:70)(cid:67)(cid:82)(cid:86)(cid:81)(cid:84)(cid:85) (cid:37)(cid:81)(cid:80)(cid:80)(cid:71)(cid:69)(cid:70)(cid:71)(cid:80)(cid:80)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2) (cid:38)(cid:91)(cid:80)(cid:67)(cid:79)(cid:75)(cid:80)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2) Figure 2 | The clathrin - coated vesicle cycle . a | The proposed five steps of clathrin - coated vesicle formation . Nucleation : FCH domain only ( FCHO ) proteins bind phosphatidylinositol - 4 , 5 - bisphosphate ( PtdIns ( 4 , 5 ) P 2 ) - rich zones of the plasma membrane and recruit EPS15 – EPS15R ( EGFR pathway substrate 15 – EPS15 - related ) and intersectins to initiate clathrin - coated pit formation by recruiting adaptor protein 2 ( AP2 ) . Cargo selection : AP2 recruits several classes of receptors directly through its μ - subunit and σ - subunit . Cargo - specific adaptors ( for example , stonin , HRB and Numb ) bind to AP2 appendage domains and recruit specific receptors to the AP2 hub . Coat assembly : clathrin triskelia are recruited by the AP2 hub and polymerize in hexagons and pentagons to form the clathrin coat around the nascent pit . Scission : the GTPase dynamin is recruited at the neck of the forming vesicle by BAR domain - containing proteins , where it self - polymerizes and , upon GTP hydrolysis , induces membrane scission . The actin machinery module can be added at this stage for actin polymerization at the neck of the pit , which can aid in vesicle production ( not shown ) . Uncoating : auxilin or cyclin G - associated kinase ( GAK ) recruit the ATPase heat shock cognate 70 ( HSC70 ) to disassemble the clathrin coat and produce an endocytic vesicle containing the cargo molecules . Synaptojanin probably facilitates this by releasing adaptor proteins from the vesicle membrane through its PtdIns lipid phosphatase activity . The components of the clathrin machinery are then freed and become available for another round of clathrin - coated vesicle formation . b | The clathrin network . The protein – protein interactions underlying the different stages of vesicle progression are shown . Major hubs are obvious because of their central location in the network and the large number of interacting molecules . They are essential for pathway progression and are denoted by the central coloured circles . Possible pathways of progression between hubs are shown with thicker lines . c | Effects of depletion of different components of the clathrin machinery . Epithelial cells expressing FCHO2 tagged with red fluorescent protein ( RFP ) , AP2 tagged on the σ 2 subunit with enhanced green fluorescent protein ( σ 2 – EGFP ) and clathrin tagged with blue fluorescent protein ( BFP ) show arrests at each successive stage in clathrin - coated pit formation after perturbation of major hubs . FCHO protein depletion through RNA interference ( RNAi ) inhibits AP2 and clathrin recruitment to the plasma membrane ( and both remain diffuse and cytosolic ) . AP2 RNAi abrogates clathrin recruitment to the plasma membrane but not FCHO2 initial focus formation ( dense red spots ) . Clathrin RNAi blocks maturation during cargo selection , when FCHO2 and AP2 are clustered ( yellow dots , arrows ) . Dynamin inhibition ( by dynasore ) blocks clathrin - coated pits at a stage just before membrane scission ( white dots , arrows ) . AAK , AP2 - associated protein kinase 1 ; ARP2 / 3 , actin - related protein 2 / 3 ; DAB2 , Disabled homologue 2 ; HIP1R , HIP1 - related ; N - WASP , neural Wiskott – Aldrich syndrome protein ; NECAP , adaptin ear - binding coat - associated protein ; SNX9 , sorting nexin 9 . (cid:38)(cid:91)(cid:80)(cid:67)(cid:79)(cid:75)(cid:80)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2) Figure 2 | The clathrin - coated vesicle cycle . a | The proposed five steps of clathrin - coated vesicle formation . Nucleation : FCH domain only ( FCHO ) proteins bind phosphatidylinositol - 4 , 5 - bisphosphate ( PtdIns ( 4 , 5 ) P 2 ) - rich zones of the plasma membrane and recruit EPS15 – EPS15R ( EGFR pathway substrate 15 – EPS15 - related ) and intersectins to initiate clathrin - coated pit formation by recruiting adaptor protein 2 ( AP2 ) . Cargo selection : AP2 recruits several classes of receptors directly through its μ - subunit and σ - subunit . Cargo - specific adaptors ( for example , stonin , HRB and Numb ) bind to AP2 appendage domains and recruit specific receptors to the AP2 hub . Coat assembly : clathrin triskelia are recruited by the AP2 hub and polymerize in hexagons and pentagons to form the clathrin coat around the nascent pit . Scission : the GTPase dynamin is recruited at the neck of the forming vesicle by BAR domain - containing proteins , where it self - polymerizes and , upon GTP hydrolysis , induces membrane scission . The actin machinery module can be added at this stage for actin polymerization at the neck of the pit , which can aid in vesicle production ( not shown ) . Uncoating : auxilin or cyclin G - associated kinase ( GAK ) recruit the ATPase heat shock cognate 70 ( HSC70 ) to disassemble the clathrin coat and produce an endocytic vesicle containing the cargo molecules . Synaptojanin probably facilitates this by releasing adaptor proteins from the vesicle membrane through its PtdIns lipid phosphatase activity . The components of the clathrin machinery are then freed and become available for another round of clathrin - coated vesicle formation . b | The clathrin network . The protein – protein interactions underlying the different stages of vesicle progression are shown . Major hubs are obvious because of their central location in the network and the large number of interacting molecules . They are essential for pathway progression and are denoted by the central coloured circles . Possible pathways of progression between hubs are shown with thicker lines . c | Effects of depletion of different components of the clathrin machinery . Epithelial cells expressing FCHO2 tagged with red fluorescent protein ( RFP ) , AP2 tagged on the σ 2 subunit with enhanced green fluorescent protein ( σ 2 – EGFP ) and clathrin tagged with blue fluorescent protein ( BFP ) show arrests at each successive stage in clathrin - coated pit formation after perturbation of major hubs . FCHO protein depletion through RNA interference ( RNAi ) inhibits AP2 and clathrin recruitment to the plasma membrane ( and both remain diffuse and cytosolic ) . AP2 RNAi abrogates clathrin recruitment to the plasma membrane but not FCHO2 initial focus formation ( dense red spots ) . Clathrin RNAi blocks maturation during cargo selection , when FCHO2 and AP2 are clustered ( yellow dots , arrows ) . Dynamin inhibition ( by dynasore ) blocks clathrin - coated pits at a stage just before membrane scission ( white dots , arrows ) . AAK , AP2 - associated protein kinase 1 ; ARP2 / 3 , actin - related protein 2 / 3 ; DAB2 , Disabled homologue 2 ; HIP1R , HIP1 - related ; N - WASP , neural Wiskott – Aldrich syndrome protein ; NECAP , adaptin ear - binding coat - associated protein ; SNX9 , sorting nexin 9 . (cid:38)(cid:91)(cid:80)(cid:67)(cid:79)(cid:75)(cid:80)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2) Figure 2 | The clathrin - coated vesicle cycle . a | The proposed five steps of clathrin - coated vesicle formation . Nucleation : FCH domain only ( FCHO ) proteins bind phosphatidylinositol - 4 , 5 - bisphosphate ( PtdIns ( 4 , 5 ) P 2 ) - rich zones of the plasma membrane and recruit EPS15 – EPS15R ( EGFR pathway substrate 15 – EPS15 - related ) and intersectins to initiate clathrin - coated pit formation by recruiting adaptor protein 2 ( AP2 ) . Cargo selection : AP2 recruits several classes of receptors directly through its μ - subunit and σ - subunit . Cargo - specific adaptors ( for example , stonin , HRB and Numb ) bind to AP2 appendage domains and recruit specific receptors to the AP2 hub . Coat assembly : clathrin triskelia are recruited by the AP2 hub and polymerize in hexagons and pentagons to form the clathrin coat around the nascent pit . Scission : the GTPase dynamin is recruited at the neck of the forming vesicle by BAR domain - containing proteins , where it self - polymerizes and , upon GTP hydrolysis , induces membrane scission . The actin machinery module can be added at this stage for actin polymerization at the neck of the pit , which can aid in vesicle production ( not shown ) . Uncoating : auxilin or cyclin G - associated kinase ( GAK ) recruit the ATPase heat shock cognate 70 ( HSC70 ) to disassemble the clathrin coat and produce an endocytic vesicle containing the cargo molecules . Synaptojanin probably facilitates this by releasing adaptor proteins from the vesicle membrane through its PtdIns lipid phosphatase activity . The components of the clathrin machinery are then freed and become available for another round of clathrin - coated vesicle formation . b | The clathrin network . The protein – protein interactions underlying the different stages of vesicle progression are shown . Major hubs are obvious because of their central location in the network and the large number of interacting molecules . They are essential for pathway progression and are denoted by the central coloured circles . Possible pathways of progression between hubs are shown with thicker lines . c | Effects of depletion of different components of the clathrin machinery . Epithelial cells expressing FCHO2 tagged with red fluorescent protein ( RFP ) , AP2 tagged on the σ 2 subunit with enhanced green fluorescent protein ( σ 2 – EGFP ) and clathrin tagged with blue fluorescent protein ( BFP ) show arrests at each successive stage in clathrin - coated pit formation after perturbation of major hubs . FCHO protein depletion through RNA interference ( RNAi ) inhibits AP2 and clathrin recruitment to the plasma membrane ( and both remain diffuse and cytosolic ) . AP2 RNAi abrogates clathrin recruitment to the plasma membrane but not FCHO2 initial focus formation ( dense red spots ) . Clathrin RNAi blocks maturation during cargo selection , when FCHO2 and AP2 are clustered ( yellow dots , arrows ) . Dynamin inhibition ( by dynasore ) blocks clathrin - coated pits at a stage just before membrane scission ( white dots , arrows ) . (cid:49)(cid:86)(cid:74)(cid:71)(cid:84)(cid:2)(cid:69)(cid:67)(cid:84)(cid:73)(cid:81) (cid:67)(cid:70)(cid:67)(cid:82)(cid:86)(cid:81)(cid:84)(cid:85) (cid:37)(cid:81)(cid:80)(cid:80)(cid:71)(cid:69)(cid:70)(cid:71)(cid:80)(cid:80)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2) (cid:38)(cid:91)(cid:80)(cid:67)(cid:79)(cid:75)(cid:80)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2) Figure 2 | The clathrin - coated vesicle cycle . a | The proposed five steps of clathrin - coated vesicle formation . Nucleation : FCH domain only ( FCHO ) proteins bind phosphatidylinositol - 4 , 5 - bisphosphate ( PtdIns ( 4 , 5 ) P 2 ) - rich zones of the plasma membrane and recruit EPS15 – EPS15R ( EGFR pathway substrate 15 – EPS15 - related ) and intersectins to initiate clathrin - coated pit formation by recruiting adaptor protein 2 ( AP2 ) . Cargo selection : AP2 recruits several classes of receptors directly through its μ - subunit and σ - subunit . Cargo - specific adaptors ( for example , stonin , HRB and Numb ) bind to AP2 appendage domains and recruit specific receptors to the AP2 hub . Coat assembly : clathrin triskelia are recruited by the AP2 hub and polymerize in hexagons and pentagons to form the clathrin coat around the nascent pit . Scission : the GTPase dynamin is recruited at the neck of the forming vesicle by BAR domain - containing proteins , where it self - polymerizes and , upon GTP hydrolysis , induces membrane scission . The actin machinery module can be added at this stage for actin polymerization at the neck of the pit , which can aid in vesicle production ( not shown ) . Uncoating : auxilin or cyclin G - associated kinase ( GAK ) recruit the ATPase heat shock cognate 70 ( HSC70 ) to disassemble the clathrin coat and produce an endocytic vesicle containing the cargo molecules . Synaptojanin probably facilitates this by releasing adaptor proteins from the vesicle membrane through its PtdIns lipid phosphatase activity . The components of the clathrin machinery are then freed and become available for another round of clathrin - coated vesicle formation . b | The clathrin network . The protein – protein interactions underlying the different stages of vesicle progression are shown . Major hubs are obvious because of their central location in the network and the large number of interacting molecules . They are essential for pathway progression and are denoted by the central coloured circles . Possible pathways of progression between hubs are shown with thicker lines . c | Effects of depletion of different components of the clathrin machinery . Epithelial cells expressing FCHO2 tagged with red fluorescent protein ( RFP ) , AP2 tagged on the σ 2 subunit with enhanced green fluorescent protein ( σ 2 – EGFP ) and clathrin tagged with blue fluorescent protein ( BFP ) show arrests at each successive stage in clathrin - coated pit formation after perturbation of major hubs . FCHO protein depletion through RNA interference ( RNAi ) inhibits AP2 and clathrin recruitment to the plasma membrane ( and both remain diffuse and cytosolic ) . AP2 RNAi abrogates clathrin recruitment to the plasma membrane but not FCHO2 initial focus formation ( dense red spots ) . Clathrin RNAi blocks maturation during cargo selection , when FCHO2 and AP2 are clustered ( yellow dots , arrows ) . Dynamin inhibition ( by dynasore ) blocks clathrin - coated pits at a stage just before membrane scission ( white dots , arrows ) . AAK , AP2 - associated protein kinase 1 ; ARP2 / 3 , actin - related protein 2 / 3 ; DAB2 , Disabled homologue 2 ; HIP1R , HIP1 - related ; N - WASP , neural Wiskott – Aldrich syndrome protein ; NECAP , adaptin ear - binding coat - associated protein ; SNX9 , sorting nexin 9 . (cid:38)(cid:91)(cid:80)(cid:67)(cid:79)(cid:75)(cid:80)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2) Figure 2 | The clathrin - coated vesicle cycle . a | The proposed five steps of clathrin - coated vesicle formation . Nucleation : FCH domain only ( FCHO ) proteins bind phosphatidylinositol - 4 , 5 - bisphosphate ( PtdIns ( 4 , 5 ) P 2 ) - rich zones of the plasma membrane and recruit EPS15 – EPS15R ( EGFR pathway substrate 15 – EPS15 - related ) and intersectins to initiate clathrin - coated pit formation by recruiting adaptor protein 2 ( AP2 ) . Cargo selection : AP2 recruits several classes of receptors directly through its μ - subunit and σ - subunit . Cargo - specific adaptors ( for example , stonin , HRB and Numb ) bind to AP2 appendage domains and recruit specific receptors to the AP2 hub . Coat assembly : clathrin triskelia are recruited by the AP2 hub and polymerize in hexagons and pentagons to form the clathrin coat around the nascent pit . Scission : the GTPase dynamin is recruited at the neck of the forming vesicle by BAR domain - containing proteins , where it self - polymerizes and , upon GTP hydrolysis , induces membrane scission . The actin machinery module can be added at this stage for actin polymerization at the neck of the pit , which can aid in vesicle production ( not shown ) . Uncoating : auxilin or cyclin G - associated kinase ( GAK ) recruit the ATPase heat shock cognate 70 ( HSC70 ) to disassemble the clathrin coat and produce an endocytic vesicle containing the cargo molecules . Synaptojanin probably facilitates this by releasing adaptor proteins from the vesicle membrane through its PtdIns lipid phosphatase activity . The components of the clathrin machinery are then freed and become available for another round of clathrin - coated vesicle formation . b | The clathrin network . The protein – protein interactions underlying the different stages of vesicle progression are shown . Major hubs are obvious because of their central location in the network and the large number of interacting molecules . They are essential for pathway progression and are denoted by the central coloured circles . Possible pathways of progression between hubs are shown with thicker lines . c | Effects of depletion of different components of the clathrin machinery . Epithelial cells expressing FCHO2 tagged with red fluorescent protein ( RFP ) , AP2 tagged on the σ 2 subunit with enhanced green fluorescent protein ( σ 2 – EGFP ) and clathrin tagged with blue fluorescent protein ( BFP ) show arrests at each successive stage in clathrin - coated pit formation after perturbation of major hubs . FCHO protein depletion through RNA interference ( RNAi ) inhibits AP2 and clathrin recruitment to the plasma membrane ( and both remain diffuse and cytosolic ) . AP2 RNAi abrogates clathrin recruitment to the plasma membrane but not FCHO2 initial focus formation ( dense red spots ) . Clathrin RNAi blocks maturation during cargo selection , when FCHO2 and AP2 are clustered ( yellow dots , arrows ) . Dynamin inhibition ( by dynasore ) blocks clathrin - coated pits at a stage just before membrane scission ( white dots , arrows ) . AAK , AP2 - associated protein kinase 1 ; ARP2 / 3 , actin - related protein 2 / 3 ; DAB2 , Disabled homologue 2 ; HIP1R , HIP1 - related ; N - WASP , neural Wiskott – Aldrich syndrome protein ; NECAP , adaptin ear - binding coat - associated protein ; SNX9 , sorting nexin 9 . (cid:49)(cid:86)(cid:74)(cid:71)(cid:84)(cid:2)(cid:69)(cid:67)(cid:84)(cid:73)(cid:81) (cid:67)(cid:70)(cid:67)(cid:82)(cid:86)(cid:81)(cid:84)(cid:85) (cid:37)(cid:81)(cid:80)(cid:80)(cid:71)(cid:69)(cid:70)(cid:71)(cid:80)(cid:80)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2) (cid:38)(cid:91)(cid:80)(cid:67)(cid:79)(cid:75)(cid:80)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2)(cid:2) Figure 2 | The clathrin - coated vesicle cycle . a | The proposed five steps of clathrin - coated vesicle formation . Nucleation : FCH domain only ( FCHO ) proteins bind phosphatidylinositol - 4 , 5 - bisphosphate ( PtdIns ( 4 , 5 ) P 2 ) - rich zones of the plasma membrane and recruit EPS15 – EPS15R ( EGFR pathway substrate 15 – EPS15 - related ) and intersectins to initiate clathrin - coated pit formation by recruiting adaptor protein 2 ( AP2 ) . Cargo selection : AP2 recruits several classes of receptors directly through its μ - subunit and σ - subunit . Cargo - specific adaptors ( for example , stonin , HRB and Numb ) bind to AP2 appendage domains and recruit specific receptors to the AP2 hub . Coat assembly : clathrin triskelia are recruited by the AP2 hub and polymerize in hexagons and pentagons to form the clathrin coat around the nascent pit . Scission : the GTPase dynamin is recruited at the neck of the forming vesicle by BAR domain - containing proteins , where it self - polymerizes and , upon GTP hydrolysis , induces membrane scission . The actin machinery module can be added at this stage for actin polymerization at the neck of the pit , which can aid in vesicle production ( not shown ) . Uncoating : auxilin or cyclin G - associated kinase ( GAK ) recruit the ATPase heat shock cognate 70 ( HSC70 ) to disassemble the clathrin coat and produce an endocytic vesicle containing the cargo molecules . Synaptojanin probably facilitates this by releasing adaptor proteins from the vesicle membrane through its PtdIns lipid phosphatase activity . The components of the clathrin machinery are then freed and become available for another round of clathrin - coated vesicle formation . b | The clathrin network . The protein – protein interactions underlying the different stages of vesicle progression are shown . Major hubs are obvious because of their central location in the network and the large number of interacting molecules . They are essential for pathway progression and are denoted by the central coloured circles . Possible pathways of progression between hubs are shown with thicker lines . c | Effects of depletion of different components of the clathrin machinery . Epithelial cells expressing FCHO2 tagged with red fluorescent protein ( RFP ) , AP2 tagged on the σ 2 subunit with enhanced green fluorescent protein ( σ 2 – EGFP ) and clathrin tagged with blue fluorescent protein ( BFP ) show arrests at each successive stage in clathrin - coated pit formation after perturbation of major hubs . FCHO protein depletion through RNA interference ( RNAi ) inhibits AP2 and clathrin recruitment to the plasma membrane ( and both remain diffuse and cytosolic ) . AP2 RNAi abrogates clathrin recruitment to the plasma membrane but not FCHO2 initial focus formation ( dense red spots ) . Clathrin RNAi blocks maturation during cargo selection , when FCHO2 and AP2 are clustered ( yellow dots , arrows ) . Dynamin inhibition ( by dynasore ) blocks clathrin - coated pits at a stage just before membrane scission ( white dots , arrows ) . AAK , AP2 - associated protein kinase 1 ; ARP2 / 3 , actin - related protein 2 / 3 ; DAB2 , Disabled homologue 2 ; HIP1R , HIP1 - related ; N - WASP , neural Wiskott – Aldrich syndrome protein ; NECAP , adaptin ear - binding coat - associated protein ; SNX9 , sorting nexin 9 . R E V I E W S 522 | AUGUST 2011 | VOLUME 12 www . nature . com / reviews / molcellbio © 2011 Macmillan Publishers Limited . All rights reserved E Figure 1 . 1 : Series of events during clathrin - mediated endocytosis . Adapted from : McMahon and Boucrot ( 2011 ) . 2 General Introduction by binding of a group of scaﬀold proteins to phosphoinositide - 4 , 5 - bisphosphate ( PIP 2 ) - rich areas of the plasma membrane which deform the membrane into a shallow pit ( Figure 1 . 1A , McMahon and Boucrot ( 2011 ) ) . This group – including F - BAR proteins , EGFR pathway substrate 15 ( EPS15 ) , intersectins and clathrin adapters ( such as adaptor protein complex 2 ( AP2 ) ) – selects and clusters cargo and nucleates actin ( Figure 1 . 1B ; Henne et al . ( 2010 ) ; Taylor et al . ( 2011 ) ; Ferguson and De Camilli ( 2012 ) ) . Clathrin binds to these adapters and forms a scaﬀold that further induces membrane curvature , deforming the membrane into a bud ( Figure 1 . 1C ) . Dynamin and N - BAR proteins ( such as endophilin ) accumulate at the neck of the pit ( Taylor et al . , 2011 ) , reducing the bud neck diameter ( Figure 1 . 1D ) . Dynamin then induces membrane ﬁssion , which liberates the vesicle from the donor membrane and completes the generation of a vesicle . The cycle is completed by auxilin or cyclin G - associated kinase ( GAK ) which recruit heat shock cognate 70 ( HSC70 ) that disassembles the clathrin coat ( Figure 1 . 1E ; Ungewickell et al . ( 1995 ) ; Schlossman et al . ( 1984 ) ) . 1 . 2 Goal Of This Thesis Work Membrane ﬁssion , the last step of the formation of a membrane vesicle , was the focus of this thesis work . Dynamin - mediated membrane ﬁssion had been reconstituted in vitro and no other proteins than dynamin were required for ﬁssion to occur ( Morlot et al . , 2012 ) . In contrast , the role of N - BAR proteins and their involvement in ﬁssion is highly debated in the ﬁeld . Strikingly , N - BAR proteins also appear at the bud neck just before vesicle ﬁssion like dynamin ( Taylor et al . , 2011 ) . Contradictory results were obtained using diﬀerent ﬁssion assays and were proposed to either activate or inhibit ﬁssion ( Farsad et al . , 2001 ; Yoshida et al . , 2004 ; Meinecke et al . , 2013 ; Neumann and Schmid , 2013 ) . The goal of my thesis was to clarify the role of the N - BAR protein endophilin in dynamin - mediated membrane ﬁssion . Chapter 2 Molecular Regulation Of Dynamin - Mediated Membrane Fission Contents 2 . 1 Dynamin . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . 3 2 . 1 . 1 Discovery And Role In Endocytosis . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . 4 2 . 1 . 2 Dynamin Structure And Assembly . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . 5 2 . 1 . 3 Dynamin Polymerisation And GTPase Activity . . . . . . . . . . . . 6 2 . 1 . 4 Mechanisms Of Dynamin - Mediated Membrane Fission . . . . . . . 8 2 . 2 The BAR Domain Proteins : Partners Of Dynamin . . . . . . . . . . 10 2 . 2 . 1 The Diﬀerent BAR Proteins : Roles In Endocytosis And Actin Functions 10 2 . 2 . 2 Amphiphysin , Endophilin And Dynamin . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . 12 2 . 3 Dynamin And The N - BAR Protein BIN1 / Amphiphysin 2 In A Muscle Disease . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . 14 2 . 3 . 1 Introduction To Article 1 . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . 14 2 . 3 . 2 Article 1 : Structual insights into the centronuclear myopathy - associated functions of BIN1 and dynamin 2 . . . . . . . 15 2 . 3 . 3 Summary Of Article 1 . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . 27 2 . 1 Dynamin Dynamin is a large GTPase of 97 kDa that mediates the membrane ﬁssion step in diﬀerent endocytic pathways . This section will give an overview of its discovery , role in endocytosis , structure , the link between dynamin polymerisation and GTPase activity and describes the currently discussed models for dynamin - mediated membrane ﬁssion . 4 Molecular Regulation Of Dynamin - Mediated Membrane Fission 2 . 1 . 1 Discovery And Role In Endocytosis Dynamin was discovered almost three decades ago as an ATPase that interacted with micro - tubules ( Shpetner and Vallee , 1999 ) , and later found to be a GTPase . In the same year , the temperature sensitive ﬂy mutant shibire was found to be unable to ﬂy or move in general at the non - permissive temperature . The reason for this block was the depletion of synaptic vesi - cles in active synapses . Clathrin - coated structures were stalled at the ﬁssion step , indicating a block in endocytosis ( Koenig and Ikeda , 1989 ) . Thus , synaptic vesicle recycling was aﬀected by the mutation , and as synaptic vesicles are needed for signal transmission , the depletion of synaptic vesicles might have caused the paralysis . The shibire gene was later found to encode the Drosophila dynamin ( van der Bliek and Meyerowitz , 1991 ) , suggesting that dynamin acts in vesicular transport . The reduction of synaptic vesicles and accumulation of clathrin - coated pits in the synaptic bulb can also be observed when knocking out the mammalian dynamin in mice ( dynamin 1 and dynamin 3 double knockout ; Figure 2 . 1 ; Raimondi et al . ( 2011 ) ; Ferguson and De Camilli ( 2012 ) ) . E Nature Reviews | Molecular Cell Biology Neck G domain‘Stalk’ ‘Stalk’ ‘Foot’ PRD Double knockout a d Resting synapse b c Presynaptic Postsynaptic Clathrin Vesicle DynaminActin Dynamin 1 Stimulated synapse P P P P Calcineurin Calcineurin Syndapin Ca 2 + Wild type with this , disruption of synaptic transmission is the most dramatic and rapid effect produced by the temperature­ sensitive inactivation of dynamin in D . melanogaster 5 , 7 , 8 . Furthermore , perturbing dynamin impairs synaptic vesicle recycling , and thus neuronal communication , in severa l experimental models 5 , 17 , 22 , 23 , 131 – 136 . The fact that all three dynamins are expressed in neu­ rons , with both dynamin 1 and dynamin 3 being expressed primarily in the nervous system , raises questions about the specific roles that each of the three dynamins has here 17 , 21 . On the basis of knockout studies , only dynamin 2 is essential for the development of the nervous system 19 . Its conditional knockout using the Cre – loxP system in early neuronal progenitors 137 , prior to the onset of expression of dynamin 1 and dynamin 3 , drastically impairs brain develop ment ( S . M . F . and P . D . C . , unpublished observa­ tions ) . However , conditional deletion of dynamin 2 in neurons at an early postnatal stage 138 does not affect mouse viability or cause any discernible neurological phenotype ( S . M . F . and P . D . C . , unpublished observations ) . This indicates that , when dynamin 1 and / or dynamin 3 are expressed , they can replace the function of dynamin 2 . Dynamin 1 and nervous system function . Dynamin 1 is present at high concentrations in the nervous syste m , is concentrated at synapses and shows markedly increased levels during synaptogenesis 17 , 18 . Additionally , dynamin 1 and several other endocytic proteins , collectively called ‘dephosphins’ ( REFS 139 – 141 ) , are constitutively phos­ phorylated in resting synapses . This dynamin phospho­ rylation depends , at least in part , on CDK5 ( REF . 119 ) , and , upon nerve stimulation , dynamin is rapidly dephos­ phorylated by the calcium­ and calmodulin­dependent phosphatase calcineurin 139 ( FIG . 4d ) ; this is predicted to facilitate dynamin inter actions with endocytic proteins to promote endocytosis 48 . The direct interaction of a dynamin 1 splice variant ( the ‘b’ C­terminal variant ) with calcineurin , through a PXIXIT­like calcineurin­ binding motif ( PRITIS ) , further emphasizes the poten­ tial physiological importance of this calcium­dependent dephosphorylation reaction for synaptic function 24 , 25 ( S . Giovedi , S . M . F . and P . D . C . , unpublished observa­ tions ) . On the basis of these considerations , dynamin 1 was expected to be essential for synaptic vesicle endocytosis . Figure 4 | Dynamin participates in synaptic vesicle recycling at neuronal synapses . a | From electron microscopy analysis , wild - type synapses ( left ) are characterized by an abundance of synaptic vesicles and very few clathrin - coated pits or clathrin - coated vesicles , which is consistent with the transient nature of clathrin - coated structures even during intense synaptic activity . At synapses that lack the great majority of their normal dynamin content ( for example , from dynamin 1 - knockout neurons or , even more strikingly , from dynamin 1 and dynamin 3 double - knockout neurons ; right ) there is a depletion of synaptic vesicles and a striking accumulation of uniformly sized clathrin - coated pits , which bud from long invaginations of the plasma membrane 17 , 22 , 145 . A small increase in the abundance of clathrin - coated pits is also observed postsynaptically , where pits are more heterogeneous in size . b | Representative electron micrograph of a presynaptic terminal from a dynamin 1 - knockout neuron . Presynaptic vesicle clusters at two synaptic junctions are very small ( regions defined by dashed lines ) , whereas clathrin - coated vesicular structures are highly abundant and occupy the bulk of the terminal . As shown by electron tomography ( see part c ) , all such structures are coated pits , although in this thin section ( ~ 60 nm ) their tubular ‘stalks’ can only be seen in few cases , and their connection with the plasma membrane cannot be appreciated 17 , 145 . c | Partial electron tomography reconstruction from dynamin 1 and dynamin 3 double - knockout nerve terminals , showing a long tubular plasma membrane invagination studded with numerous individual clathrin - coated pits . The arrow indicates the opening of this tubular structure at the peripheral presynaptic plasma membrane . d | In resting synapses , the Pro - rich domain ( PRD ) of dynamin 1 is phosphorylated , preventing association with syndapin . Upon stimulation and increased cytosolic calcium concentration , the protein phosphatase calcineurin , which directly binds a dynamin 1 splice variant ( xb ) , dephosphorylates dynamin 1 , allowing its interaction with syndapin . This regulated interaction is thought to promote synaptic vesicle endocytosis at times of elevated neuronal activity . This dynamin phospho­ rylation depends , at least in part , on CDK5 ( REF . 119 ) , and , upon nerve stimulation , dynamin is rapidly dephos­ phorylated by the calcium­ and calmodulin­dependent phosphatase calcineurin 139 ( FIG . 4d ) ; this is predicted to facilitate dynamin inter actions with endocytic proteins to promote endocytosis 48 . The direct interaction of a dynamin 1 splice variant ( the ‘b’ C­terminal variant ) with calcineurin , through a PXIXIT­like calcineurin­ binding motif ( PRITIS ) , further emphasizes the poten­ tial physiological importance of this calcium­dependent dephosphorylation reaction for synaptic function 24 , 25 ( S . Giovedi , S . M . F . and P . D . C . , unpublished observa­ tions ) . On the basis of these considerations , dynamin 1 was expected to be essential for synaptic vesicle endocytosis . Figure 4 | Dynamin participates in synaptic vesicle recycling at neuronal synapses . a | From electron microscopy analysis , wild - type synapses ( left ) are characterized by an abundance of synaptic vesicles and very few clathrin - coated pits or clathrin - coated vesicles , which is consistent with the transient nature of clathrin - coated structures even during intense synaptic activity . At synapses that lack the great majority of their normal dynamin content ( for example , from dynamin 1 - knockout neurons or , even more strikingly , from dynamin 1 and dynamin 3 double - knockout neurons ; right ) there is a depletion of synaptic vesicles and a striking accumulation of uniformly sized clathrin - coated pits , which bud from long invaginations of the plasma membrane 17 , 22 , 145 . A small increase in the abundance of clathrin - coated pits is also observed postsynaptically , where pits are more heterogeneous in size . b | Representative electron micrograph of a presynaptic terminal from a dynamin 1 - knockout neuron . Presynaptic vesicle clusters at two synaptic junctions are very small ( regions defined by dashed lines ) , whereas clathrin - coated vesicular structures are highly abundant and occupy the bulk of the terminal . As shown by electron tomography ( see part c ) , all such structures are coated pits , although in this thin section ( ~ 60 nm ) their tubular ‘stalks’ can only be seen in few cases , and their connection with the plasma membrane cannot be appreciated 17 , 145 . c | Partial electron tomography reconstruction from dynamin 1 and dynamin 3 double - knockout nerve terminals , showing a long tubular plasma membrane invagination studded with numerous individual clathrin - coated pits . The arrow indicates the opening of this tubular structure at the peripheral presynaptic plasma membrane . d | In resting synapses , the Pro - rich domain ( PRD ) of dynamin 1 is phosphorylated , preventing association with syndapin . Upon stimulation and increased cytosolic calcium concentration , the protein phosphatase calcineurin , which directly binds a dynamin 1 splice variant ( xb ) , dephosphorylates dynamin 1 , allowing its interaction with syndapin . This regulated interaction is thought to promote synaptic vesicle endocytosis at times of elevated neuronal activity . By contrast , reports of variability in the size and dynamic behaviour of clathrin structures in mammalian cells have raised questions about the underlying biological significance of the different populations and about the regulatory mechanisms responsible for this heterogeneity . Furthermore , this heterogeneity has limited the ability to perform a global analysis of protein dynamics to detect the phenotypes that are caused when endocytic protein functions are impaired . Our data suggest that conventional overexpression - based methods in mammalian cells contribute to heterogeneity in the size and dynamics of clathrin - coated structures , thus warranting the use of genome - edited cells for re - examination of the effects of cargo , cell physiology and function - perturbing manipulations on endocytic dynamics and productivity . ZFN - mediated genome editing has several advantages over conven - tional methods for generating cell lines that stably express fluorescent fusion proteins . First , conventional methods require selection of a single splice variant for study and , consequently , dominant expression of a sin - gle isoform . Moreover , these methods result in transgene overexpression , leading to total protein levels ( comprising both tagged and untagged forms ) that are significantly higher than in wild - type cells . Although transient overexpression methods can generate cells that express a fusion protein closer to physiological levels , they often result in heterogene - ous cell - to - cell protein expression levels , necessitating experimental bias in the selection of ‘low - expression’ cells for study . By contrast , a ZFN - mediated strategy allows for creation of single - or multiple - allele tagged cell lines for greater control of a tagged protein’s expression level . Furthermore , our tagging strategy preserves native RNA splicing , ena - bling the analysis of protein isoforms at physiological stoichiometry and levels . Although such an approach precludes an analysis of individual splice variants , alternative ZFNs and donors could be readily designed to achieve exclusive expression of a desired isoform at endogenous levels . Although the need to perturb a biological process to observe it is a general shortcoming of experimental research , we believe that our studies strike a balance between modifying a cell to faithfully report on its biology and retaining its natural state . In particular , the ability to engineer isogenic human cells using ZFN technology 21 , 30 , 31 in a manner that has been the gold standard in budding and fission yeast for decades has the potential to transform the way that researchers study dynamic processes . While there is a big family of dynamin - related proteins in pro - and eukaryotes with roles in membrane remodelling , the most studied members are the classical dynamins from mammals . Mammals have three dynamin paralogs with 70 % sequence identity and same domain structure ( see Section 2 . 1 . 2 ) , each of the paralogs with several splice variants ( UniProt ) . Dynamin 1 is by far the predominant variant in the brain and is neuron - speciﬁc ( Scaife and Margolis , 1990 ; Sontag et al . , 1994 ; Powell and Robinson , 1995 ) . Dynamin 2 is ubiquitously expressed and considered to be responsible for house - keeping endocytosis ( Cook et al . , 1994 ; Sontag et al . , 1994 ; Diatloﬀ - Zito et al . , 1995 ) . Dynamin 3 is expressed in neurons , lung and testis ( Nakata et al . , 1993 ; Cook et al . , 1996 ) . When observed by total internal reﬂection ﬂuorescence ( TIRF ) microscopy , dynamin appears as transient punctae that colocalise with clathrin ( Figure 2 . 2 ; Doyon et al . ( 2011 ) ) . The lifetime of the punctae was in the range of 20 – 40 seconds ( Doyon et al . , 2011 ) , depending on the exact genome editing . Dynamin accumulated massively a few seconds before vesicle ﬁssion ( Taylor et al . ( 2011 ) , see also Figure 2 . 9 ) , suggesting a role in the ﬁssion step . 2 . 1 . 2 Dynamin Structure And Assembly The domain structure of a dynamin monomer and the structure of the dynamin 3 tetramer ( Reubold et al . , 2015 ) are shown in Figure 2 . 3 . Dynamin contains a GTPase ( G ) domain ( orange ) that hydrolyses GTP . The pleckstrin homology ( PH ) domain binds to the membrane through a speciﬁc interaction with phosphatidylinositol - 4 , 5 - bisphosphate ( PIP 2 ) . The stalk regions mediate dimerisation ( Figure 2 . 3 , interface 2 ) , tetramerisation ( Muhlberg et al . ( 1997 ) , Figure 2 . 3 , interfaces 1 and 3 , Reubold et al . ( 2015 ) ) and thus oligomerisation . The bundle signalling element ( BSE ) is a ﬂexible linker that connects the G domain with the rest of the protein . The proline - rich domain ( PRD ) mediates interactions between dynamin and SH3 - domain containing proteins such as certain BAR proteins ( see Section 2 . 2 ) . 6 Molecular Regulation Of Dynamin - Mediated Membrane Fission A B G domain BSE BSE BSE stalk / middle PH stalk / GED PRD LETTER doi : 10 . 1038 / nature14880 Crystal structure of the dynamin tetramer Thomas F . Reubold 1 * , Katja Faelber 2 * , Nuria Plattner 3 , York Posor 4 { , Katharina Ketel 4 , Ute Curth 1 , 5 , Jeanette Schlegel 2 , Roopsee Anand 1 , Dietmar J . Manstein 1 , 5 , Frank Noe´ 3 , Volker Haucke 4 , 6 , Oliver Daumke 2 , 6 & Susanne Eschenburg 1 The mechanochemical protein dynamin is the prototype of the dynamin superfamily of large GTPases , which shape and remodel membranes in diverse cellular processes 1 . Dynamin forms predo - minantly tetramers in the cytosol , which oligomerize at the neck of clathrin - coated vesicles to mediate constriction and subsequent scission of the membrane 1 . Previous studies have described the architecture of dynamin dimers 2 , 3 , but the molecular determinants for dynamin assembly and its regulation have remained unclear . Here we present the crystal structure of the human dynamin tetramer in the nucleotide - free state . Combining structural data with mutational studies , oligomerization measurements and Markov state models of molecular dynamics simulations , we sug - gest a mechanism by which oligomerization of dynamin is linked to the release of intramolecular autoinhibitory interactions . We elu - cidate how mutations that interfere with tetramer formation and autoinhibition can lead to the congenital muscle disorders Charcot – Marie – Tooth neuropathy 4 and centronuclear myopathy 5 , respectively . Notably , the bent shape of the tetramer explains how dynamin assembles into a right - handed helical oligomer of defined diameter , which has direct implications for its function in mem - brane constriction . The three highly conserved vertebrate isoforms of dynamin contain five distinct domains ( Extended Data Fig . 1a ) : an N - terminal GTPase ( G ) domain mediating nucleotide binding and hydrolysis , a bundle signalling element ( BSE ) , a stalk , a pleckstrin homology ( PH ) domain involved in lipid binding , and a proline - rich domain ( PRD ) mediating interactions with scaffolding proteins containing BAR - and SH3 - domains 6 . To exert its function in clathrin - mediated endocytosis ( CME ) , dynamin assembles via the stalks into a helical array surround - ing the necks of invaginating clathrin - coated pits 7 , 8 . Dimerization of GTP - bound G domains from neighbouring helical rungs induces GTP hydrolysis 9 . The ensuing conformational changes are thought to be transmitted from the G domain via the BSE to the stalk , resulting in a sliding motion of adjacent helix rungs , concomitant helix constric - tion 10 , and eventually membrane scission . The inherent tendency to form large assemblies at high protein concentrations has hampered crystallization of dynamin in the past . ( 2015 ) . 2 . 1 . 3 Dynamin Polymerisation And GTPase Activity Dynamin forms polymers onto membrane templates ( Sweitzer and Hinshaw , 1998 ) . In low - salt conditions , dynamin self - assembles into rings ( Hinshaw and Schmid , 1995 ) . The polymers on membrane templates are right - handed and mediated by interfaces 1 and 3 ( Figure 2 . 3 , Reubold et al . ( 2015 ) ) . The G domains from adjacent helix turns interact in the polymer ( Figure 2 . 4 , lower middle and right ) . Assembly of dynamin into higher - order polymers on membrane B Nature Reviews | Molecular Cell Biology N e c k N e c k N e c k 1 301 520 627 751 864 GTPase Middle PH GED PRD G domain ‘Stalk’ ‘Stalk’ ‘Foot’ PRD a Dynamin 1 b d c e Polymerization of dynamin helix Membrane ﬁssion GTP - dependent dimerization of G domains , GTP hydrolysis and resulting membrane constriction G domain GTP Neck ‘Stalk’‘Foot’ 1 3 2 2 90° The G domain and BSE . The G domain sits on a helical bundle , known as the bundle signalling element ( BSE ) 30 or neck 40 , which is formed by three helices derived from sequences at the N­terminal and C­terminal sides of the G domain and from the C­terminal region of the GED , respectively ( FIG . 2 ) . Consistent with the idea that this region of the GED is in close physical proximity with , and is functionally linked to , the G domain , a screen for suppressor mutations of a mutation in the G domain of D . melanogaster dynamin identified a mutation within the GED C terminus 41 . The BSE is followed by a stalk , which is composed of helices from the middle domain and the N­terminal region of the GED 30 – 33 , and a PH domain 42 , which forms the vertex or ‘foot’ of the stalk hairpin and binds membranes . The PRD , which is expected to be unfolded , emerges at the boundary between the BSE and the G domain , most likely project­ ing away from the membrane , where it might interact with other proteins . Dimerization through the stalk . The stalk of dynamin dimerizes in a cross­like fashion ( FIG . 2a , b ) to yield a dynamin dimer in which the two G domains are oriented in opposite directions 30 – 33 ( FIG . 2b ) . This dimer is the basic dynamin unit and is different from the additional dimer­ ization interface that is generated by the interaction of two G domains ( FIG . 2b , c ) , which is discussed below . Phospholipid association through the PH domain . The PH domain binds acidic phospholipids in the cytosolic leaflet of the plasma membrane , and phosphatidyl­ inositol­4 , 5­bisphosphate ( PtdIns ( 4 , 5 ) P 2 ) in particular , via a positively charged surface at the foot of the dynamin hairpin 42 , 43 . PH­domain mutants that impair phospho­ inositide binding exert dominant­negative effects on clathrin­mediated endocytosis 44 , 45 . The binding between the isolated dynamin PH domain and phosphoinositides is of very modest affinity ( > 1 mM ) , but this membrane interaction is strengthened by charge­dependent asso­ ciation with other negatively charged phospholipids and by avidity afforded by dynamin polymerization 43 – 46 . A hydrophobic loop emerging from the PH domain may promote membrane interactions and may also have curvatur e­generatin g or ­sensing properties 28 , 47 . Coordinating dynamin function through the PRD . The PRD contains an array of PXXP amino acid motifs , which interact with many SH3 domain­containing proteins ( see Supplementary information S1 ( table ) ) to localize dynamin at endocytic sites and coordinate dynamin’s function with these other factors during endocytosis 48 – 51 . Accordingly , dynamin lacking the PRD cannot rescue endocytic defects in dynamin­knockout fibroblasts 19 . The PRD – SH3 interactions are typically of moderate affinity , but the presence of multiple SH3­binding motifs in the PRD and multiple SH3 domain­containing pro­ teins at endocytic sites , as well as the polymeric state of these proteins , results in a significant avidity effect , which enhances the ability of such interactions to concentrate dynamin . At least some interactions of the dynamin PRD are regulate d by phosphorylation 48 . Adapted from : Ferguson and De Camilli ( 2012 ) . 2 . 1 Dynamin 7 templates which involve the interaction of G domains stimulates dynamin’s GTPase activity 1000 fold ( Stowell et al . , 1999 ) . The precise role of the GTPase activity by the G domains for dynamin - mediated ﬁssion is still highly debated ( Antonny et al . ( 2016 ) and next section , 2 . 1 . 4 ) , but there is consensus concerning the fact that GTP hydrolysis is required for ﬁssion to occur . Dynamin is able to induce membrane curvature via its polymerisation properties , as well in vivo where vesicle necks are wider when dynamin is absent from the neck ( Newton et al . , 2006 ; Shupliakov , 1997 ) , as in vitro ( Sweitzer and Hinshaw , 1998 ; Takei et al . , 1999 ; Roux et al . , 2010 ) . Cryo - EM allowed to visualise the structures of dynamin polymers on membrane tubes ( Figure 2 . 5 ) together with the dimensions of the dynamin polymer and the underlying membrane tube . Diﬀerent geometries were obtained for diﬀerent nucleotide states and dynamin constructs . In the nucleotide - free state , the dynamin helix has an outer diameter of 50 nm with a helical pitch in the order of 10 – 20 nm and a membrane mid - plane diameter of 20 nm ( Takei et al . , 1998 ; Sweitzer and Hinshaw , 1998 ; Takei et al . , 1999 ; Danino et al . , 2004 ; Chen et al . , 2004 ) . ∆ PRD - dynamin in the GMPPCP - bound polymer is in the constricted state with an inner membrane lumen of only 7 nm diameter ( Zhang and Hinshaw , 2001 ) . The number of dynamin dimers per helical turn is only slightly reduced from 14 to 13 . 2 dimers ( non - constricted and Dynamin is a GTP hydrolysis - dependent , membrane fission catalyzer The essential function of dynamin is to use energy from GTP hydro - lysis to sever membrane tubules . Fission of clathrin - coated pits from the plasma membrane is defective at neuronal synapses of mice lacking dynamin 1 , or both dynamins 1 and 3 ( Ferguson et al , 2007 ; Raimondi et al , 2011 ) and in embryonic fibroblasts from mice with conditional double ( Ferguson et al , 2009 ) or triple deletions of dynamin genes ( Park et al , 2013 ) . Mutants with reduced GTPase activity delay or block endocytosis of transferrin ( Marks et al , 2001 ; Boll et al , 2004 ; Song et al , 2004 ) and prolong the residence time of clathrin / dynamin at the plasma membrane ( Taylor et al , 2011 ; Kural et al , 2012 ) . GTPase - defective mutants have dominant nega - tive phenotypes when they co - assemble with wild - type proteins in overexpression experiments ( Damke et al , 1994 ) . The mechanism of dynamin - mediated membrane fission has been studied by reconstitution with purified components . GTP hydrolysis is consistently required for membrane fission in these reconstituted systems ( Sweitzer & Hinshaw , 1998 ; Roux et al , 2006 ; Bashkirov et al , 2008 ; Pucadyil & Schmid , 2008 ; Morlot et al , 2012 ; Shnyrova et al , 2013 ; Mattila et al , 2015 ) . Membrane tension , which can be provided by adhesion of the membrane tubes to the substrate , facilitates the reaction ( see also below ) ( Sweitzer & Hinshaw , 1998 ; Danino et al , 2004 ; Roux et al , 2006 ; Boulant et al , 2011 ; Morlot et al , 2012 ) . As in membrane fusion , dynamin - mediated fission proceeds through a hemi - fission state where the inner leaflet of the tube disappears ( see Fig 1B ) , leaving a connect - ing neck made of a single lipid monolayer wrapped in a cylindrical micelle ( Bashkirov et al , 2008 ; Morlot et al , 2012 ; Shnyrova et al , 2013 ; Mattila et al , 2015 ) . Dynamin helices constrict in the presence of GTP There is broad agreement that a key property of the dynamin helical oligomer is its ability to constrict in the presence of GTP .
