Hohendahl et al . / Journal of Structural Biology 196 ( 2016 ) 37 – 47 43 mutation , CME functions normally , while it is slightly impaired in MEFs homozygous for these mutations ( homozygous mice die after birth ) ( Durieux et al . , 2010 ) . These ﬁndings show that the disease is probably not related to the function of dynamin in CME , whose alteration causes embryonic lethality , and that these mutations seem to have very little effect on CME . Moreover , a gain of function of dynamin 2 in CME is likely to have no physiological impact , as CME would just go faster . However , a recent study has shown a slight impairment in clathrin - independent EGF , cholera toxin uptake and EGFR downregulation as well as a defect in trafﬁcking of p75 receptor from the Golgi to the plasma membrane in stable cell lines expressing physiological levels of the hyperactive dyna - min 2 mutations R465W and E368K ( Liu et al . , 2011 ) . This may cause signalling deregulation in these patients , which may account for the severity of some forms . As a conclusion , the biochemical , biological and clinical analysis of CNM - related dynamin 2 mutations has shown that they have a global gain of function with no dramatic impact on the ubiquitous functions of dynamin 2 in CME . The pathology must therefore arise from the alteration of another function of dynamin 2 delimited to a muscle - speciﬁc role . 3 . 2 . Gain of function dynamin 2 mutations alter a tissue - speciﬁc balance The fact that none of the ubiquitous functions of dynamin 2 are defective in a heterozygous background of CNM - related dynamin 2 mutations leads to consider tissue - speciﬁc functions of dynamin 2 in the muscle . In muscle ﬁbres , dynamin 2 has been found along the Z - line , co - localizing with a - actinin and desmin . Dynamin 2 is located in close proximity to dihydropyridine receptor ( DHPR ) , a marker of T - tubules ( Cowling et al . , 2011 ; Durieux et al . , 2010 ) , which suggests that dynamin 2 , like BIN1 , could be implicated in T - tubule biogenesis . The presence of dynamin 2 on T - tubules still has to be shown . The analysis of CNM - related dynamin 2 muta - tions in animal models and in cells strongly implicates that the hyperactivation of dynamin 2 is deleterious to the maintenance and stabilization of T - tubules and triads , suggesting a tissue - speciﬁc role of dynamin in muscles related to T - tubule and triad shaping . The expression of human dynamin 2 carrying the muta - tion R465W in adult mice results in a decrease in muscle mass due to the appearance of atrophic ﬁbres . Histological analysis showed misalignment of Z - lines and triad defects such as abnor - mally shaped T - tubules and a swollen sarcoplasmic reticulum ( Cowling et al . , 2011 ) . In heterozygous mice for the same mutation , a slight disorganization of T - tubules , sarcoplasmic reticulum and an increase in cytosolic Ca 2 + are also observed , although defects in the triad structure are milder ( Durieux et al . , 2010 ) . Similar results have been obtained in non - mammalian organ - isms , supporting a conserved role of dynamin 2 in T - tubule devel - opment through evolution . In larvae of transgenic Drosophila ectopically expressing one of the human dynamin 2 mutations R465W , A618T or S619L in the muscle displayed fragmented T - tubules even when expressed later in development when T - tubules are already formed ( Chin et al . , 2015 ) . In zebraﬁsh , where extensive disorganization of triad structures and T - tubule fragmentation can be observed when the human dynamin 2 S619L mutant is expressed during development , these defects led to impaired excitation - contraction coupling ( Gibbs et al . , 2014 ) . Altogether , these results suggest a tissue - speciﬁc function of dynamin 2 in the establishment of the T - tubule structures in mus - cle ﬁbres . T - tubules are a result of plasma membrane tubulation carried out most probably by caveolin - 3 and BIN1 . Dynamin 2 could either serve as a scaffolding protein as it is able to form a more rigid scaffold then N - BAR proteins ( Frost et al . , 2008 ) , which could help the maintenance and the resistance of the T - tubule system needed for muscle contraction . An alternative hypothesis is that dynamin 2 could be involved in T - tubule length regulation through membrane ﬁssion . Another hint of a possible function of dynamin in T - tubule shaping comes from the BIN1 mutant K575X : its impairment of the SH3 domain , thus loss of interaction with dynamin 2 , could account for its pathological outcome in patients ( Nicot et al . , 2007 ) . However , the ﬁssion activity of dynamin 2 must be blocked or tightly regulated to play this role , otherwise dynamin would exces - sively cut these T - tubules , leading to a fragmented T - tubule sys - tem . In a wild type background , dynamin 2 ﬁssion activity should be somehow inhibited or regulated at the T - tubule . This also explains why gain - of function mutations would have a dra - matic effect speciﬁcally at the T - tubule , as enhancing the ﬁssion activity of dynamin 2 would cause disruption of the T - tubule sys - tem . But how dynamin 2 ﬁssion activity would be speciﬁcally inhibited at the T - tubule ? As described in the following , this may arise from its speciﬁc interaction with BIN1 . 3 . 3 . Interplay between dynamin , BIN1 and MTM1 functions in T - tubule biogenesis BIN1 may speciﬁcally recruit dynamin 2 to the T - tubule system ( Lee et al . , 2002 ) and inhibit its ﬁssion activity . Supporting this assertion , other N - BAR proteins such as endophilin and amphiphy - sin regulate dynamin’s ﬁssion activity , but the nature of the regu - lation ( activation versus inhibition ) seemed to vary for different N - BAR proteins and in different conditions ( Farsad et al . , 2001 ; Meinecke et al . , 2013 ; Neumann and Schmid , 2013 ; Takei et al . , 1999 ) . In some experiments ( Boucrot et al . , 2012 ; Farsad et al . , 2001 ) , N - BAR proteins associated with dynamin have displayed an inhibitory action on dynamin ﬁssion activity . Thus , one could postulate that BIN1 and dynamin 2 form a heteropolymer that would block dynamin 2’s ability to sever the membrane . However , this effect has not been reproducibly established , and contradic - tory results have been obtained ( Meinecke et al . , 2013 ; Neumann and Schmid , 2013 ; Takei et al . , 1999 ; Yoshida et al . , 2004 ) . In muscle ﬁbres expressing CNM - related dynamin 2 mutations , the abnormal hyperactivity of these mutants could overcome the inhibition of dynamin - ﬁssion activity , shifting the equilibrium between dynamin 2 scaffolding with a controlled membrane ﬁs - sion function towards unregulated membrane ﬁssion . This would result in the fragmented and abnormally shaped T - tubules , as observed in the animal models expressing hyperactive dynamin 2 mutations ( Chin et al . , 2015 ; Gibbs et al . , 2014 ) . Evidences supporting this model come from experiments in cells . Upon overexpression of BIN1 ( or other N - BAR proteins ) in cultured cells , an extensive membrane tubulation is observed . This effect can be counteracted by overexpressing dynamin ( Itoh et al . , 2005 ) or by expressing a CNM - related hyperactive mutation ( Chin et al . , 2015 ; Gibbs et al . , 2014 ) . In these examples , the plasma membrane tubulation is the result of an imbalance between the tubulation activity of BIN1 ( higher ) and the ﬁssion activity of dyna - min ( lower ) : the balance can be restored by either increasing the amount of dynamin , or by expressing a dynamin mutant with increased activity . Also , as described above , mutations in the SH3 domain of BIN1 could impair its interaction with dynamin 2 , releasing dynamin’s inhibition . In these mutants , dynamin 2 would not be inhibited enough to allow for proper T - tubule maintenance . However , as BIN1 also participates in the recruitment of dynamin 2 to the T - tubule system , together with phosphoinositides , one may question if the reduced recruitment of dynamin 2 in the SH3 BIN1 mutants may counteract the reduced inhibition of dynamin ﬁssion activity . In this context , the role of the phosphoinositides may be essential to understand the mechanism of the disease . Myotubularin , the 44 A . Hohendahl et al . / Journal of Structural Biology 196 ( 2016 ) 37 – 47 third protein causing CNM when mutated , may be critical as it is a 3 - phosphatase that can interact with BIN1 . In Royer et al . ( 2013 ) , the authors found that myotubularin ( MTM1 ) binds BIN1 in vitro and in skeletal muscle . Similar to the effect of binding of dynamin’s PRD domain to BIN1 , the authors propose that MTM1 may help dynamin and BIN1 tubulating activity . It would also require MTM1’s phosphatase activity . MTM1 is a 3 - phosphatase and its substrates are PI ( 3 ) P and PI ( 3 , 5 ) P 2 . As BIN1 was shown to bind to PI ( 5 ) P as well as PI ( 4 , 5 ) P 2 in contrast to PI ( 3 , 5 ) P 2 ( Fugier et al . , 2011 ; Lee et al . , 2002 ; Picas et al . , 2014 ) , one can hypothesize that MTM1 might promote the formation of 5 - phosphate phosphoinosi - tides , such as PI ( 5 ) P and PI ( 4 , 5 ) P 2 , by increasing the level of their precursors ( PI and PI ( 5 ) P ) . These 5 - phosphate phosphoinositides will then recruit BIN1 and dynamin to the plasma or T - tubule membrane . Furthermore , Royer et al . ( 2013 ) observed that both Q573X and K575X BIN1 mutants have an increased interaction with MTM1 in vitro . A plausible mechanism would thus be that the same SH3 mutants of BIN1 have a decreased interaction with dynamin and an increased interaction with MTM1 . The defective recruit - ment of dynamin by the BIN1 SH3 mutant could thus be compen - sated by the increase of 5 - phosphate phosphoinositides resulting from a higher recruitment of MTM1 to BIN1 structures . However in this case , dynamin’s ﬁssion activity would not be inhibited , since the interaction with BIN1 is lost , and would thus lead to a dis - rupted T - tubule system . The BIN1 - MTM1 interaction is also interesting when compared with other N - BAR / phosphatase pairs : for example , endophilin physically interacts with and recruits the lipid phosphatase synap - tojanin to the membrane of clathrin - coated pits ( Perera et al . , 2006 ) . In the synaptojanin - endophilin case , the synaptojanin recruitment is proposed to result in a decrease of the PI ( 4 , 5 ) P 2 con - centration and to allow for ﬁssion and uncoating of clathrin - coated pits ( Perera et al . , 2006 ) . The striking difference to the synaptojanin - endophilin pair is that MTM1 recruitment by BIN1 should , via increasing the concentration of the PI ( 4 , 5 ) P 2 precursor , lead to an increase of PI ( 4 , 5 ) P 2 , which in turn would recruit more BIN1 and dynamin . This opposite effect correlates nicely with the idea that the scaffold which stabilises T - tubules would have a pos - itive feedback loop where the scaffold proteins increase their respective recruitment , whereas the scaffold and coat implicated in the formation of a clathrin - coated vesicle is temporary . 4 . General conclusions We have reviewed in this article how different groups of muta - tions disturb the structure and function of BIN1 , leading to CNM . BIN1 mutations in the amphipathic helix could decrease BIN1’s scaffolding properties on membrane tubes . Mutations in the tip region of the BAR domain dimer may decrease BIN1’s tubulation properties . Also in the case of splice - site mutations resulting in a loss of the PI motif , BIN1 tubulates less and the T - tubule formation and / or maintenance is impaired . In contrast , mutations in the SH3 domain do not impair BIN1’s curvature inducing features but might affect both dynamin and MTM1 levels at the T - tubules . CNM - related mutations in dynamin 2 are hyperactive and thus correspond to a gain of function . As long as they are heterozygous , they cannot impair clathrin - mediated endocytosis because they maintain the ability to mediate membrane ﬁssion and their action is regulated by redundant factors and regulators . In T - tubule bio - genesis and maintenance , it is primarily the membrane scaffolding and tubulation activities or a moderate ﬁssion activity of dynamin that are at work . T - tubule biogenesis thus requires a down regula - tion of dynamin 2’s intrinsic ﬁssion activity . Thus , dynamin 2 mutations that have increased ﬁssion activity which are not harmful for CME , probably cause massive problems in the T - tubule system because of their inability to be down regulated . Thus , the balance between membrane tubulating and ﬁssion activ - ities of dynamin is crucial for the T - tubule biogenesis . Given that CNM - associated dynamin mutants are hyperactive and BIN1 mutants have a decrease - of - function , CNMs are one example where an N - BAR protein seems to negatively regulate dynamin’s ﬁssion activity . To test this hypothesis , one could over - express dynamin 2 GTPase defective mutants in cells with CNM - associated BIN1 mutations . If this rescues the low - function BIN1 phenotype ( fragmented T - tubules ) , this would clearly speak for a role of BIN1 in preventing dynamin from cutting T - tubules . Fitting with this theory , a patent has been published for the idea to treat CNM patients with dynamin inhibitors ( Laporte and Cowling , European Patent EP2862928A1 ) . Another interesting matter of the CNMs is its tissue - speciﬁcity to muscles , while other cellular functions seemed unaffected by the CNM mutations , even though most of the mutations affect ubiquitously expressed exons of BIN1 and dynamin 2 . We hypoth - esize that the tissue - speciﬁcity of the pathology is due to the fact that T - tubules are one of few cases where membrane tubules are formed in cells and are required to be incredibly stable over time , while they represent ideal targets for dynamin’s ﬁssion activity . Thus a tight regulation of the levels of BIN1 and dynamin , as well as of the balance between their speciﬁc activities is required in the T - tubule system , with very little redundancy as compared to the CME system . Most probably , the triple complex between dynamin 2 , BIN1 and MTM1 is at the heart of this balance between mem - brane tubulation and ﬁssion activity , as many of the mutations found in these three proteins affect the protein - protein interaction domains . Overall , if membrane deformation properties are too low , the T - tubule formation is impaired . If ﬁssion activity is too high , T - tubule are snapped too early after formation . Hohendahl et al . / Journal of Structural Biology 196 ( 2016 ) 37 – 47 47 2 . 3 Dynamin And The N - BAR Protein BIN1 / Amphiphysin 2 In A Muscle Disease 27 2 . 3 . 3 Summary Of Article 1 In this review , we analysed all currently known centronuclear myopathy ( CNM ) linked mutations in the BIN1 / amphiphysin 2 and dynamin 2 proteins on a structural and functional level . We used the available knowledge from in vitro experiments and from experiments using cell culture or entire organisms , as well as clinical descriptions and histopathological analyses from CNM patients . A table for each protein summarises the position in the amino acid sequence , exon , domain , disease segregation , disease severity , onset , main functional consequence ( as far as known ) and the reference paper of the discovery of the mutation . For each protein , the position of the mutated amino acids is shown in the available 3D protein structure . For dynamin 2 , the currently known functional consequences of the mutated amino acids are similar , independently of the positioning of the mutation , while for BIN1 the domain which is aﬀected by the mutation changes the structural and functional consequences . This is why for BIN1 , the mutations are grouped by the domain which is aﬀected . Mutations in the N - terminal amphipathic helix of BIN1 suggested the importance of this helix for BIN1’s scaﬀolding properties , which are impaired when mutated . Mutations in the BAR domain itself seemed to decrease BIN1 - induced tubulation . Also when the PI motif is lost in a splice - site mutant for the respective exon , BIN1 tubulates less , and on top T - tubule formation and / or stability is af - fected . Interestingly , the PI motif is muscle - speciﬁc . All the observed changes in tubulation and scaﬀolding were in line with the phenotype in patients and dogs that the T - tubule network was abnormally disrupted . T - tubules are tubular structures which connect the plasma membrane of the muscle ﬁbre ( myocyte ) with the actin ﬁbres . T - tubules transmit the arriving depolarisation upon the arrival of an action potential deep into the cell , allowing for rapid muscle contraction upon action potentials . Mutations in the SH3 domain were , on the other hand , not observed to change tubulation or scaﬀolding properties , ﬁtting with the knowledge that the BAR domain and not the SH3 domain interacts with the membrane . Instead , these mutants showed a diﬀerent interaction with dynamin 2 , correlating with the knowledge that SH3 domains is the domain that interacts with dynamin and other PRD - domain containing proteins . For dynamin 2 , the ﬁrst idea that endocytosis would be aﬀected due to the mutations did not seem to be true in patients . As CNM dynamin 2 mutants are hyperactive , dynamin can still mediate ﬁssion ( see Section 2 . 1 . 4 ) and its action is , at least concerning endocytosis , enough regulated by other factors to be functional . As patients with DNM2 mutations have a disrupted T - tubule system and as the mutations are hyperactive , dynamin’s original role in the T - tubule system does not seem to be membrane ﬁssion , but in contrast the stabilisation of T - tubules . The review puts the hypothesis forward that wild - type dynamin’s ﬁssion properties are inhibited by BIN1 . This intracellular balance is disturbed by either decreasing BIN’s membrane binding and scaﬀolding properties ( BIN1 CNM mutants ) or by increasing dynamin’s activity ( DNM2 CNM mutants ) , leading in both cases to impairment of T - tubule formation or stability and the CNM speciﬁc symptoms of muscle weakness and muscle waisting . Summary Of Article 3 ) . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . 35 3 . 2 . 5 Measuring Dynamin - Mediated Membrane Fission Rates . . . . . . . 37 3 . 1 Basics Of Membrane Physics 3 . 1 . 1 Membranes Are 2D Fluid Thin Sheets Deﬁned By Their Tension And Rigidity The typical physical model of a biological lipid membrane is a ﬂuid thin sheet . For membranes whose width and length are in a considerably higher order of magnitude than the bilayer thick - ness ( µ m vs . nm range ) , one can neglect the bilayer thickness and consider the membrane as a 2D surface . Membranes can be deformed in three diﬀerent ways ( Figure 3 . 1 ) . Stretch - ing deﬁnes an area expansion during the application of isotropic forces that ﬁrst result in the unfolding of excess area stored in membrane ﬂuctuations ( entropic regime ) and then in an increase in the distance between lipid headgroups ( enthalpic regime ) . Membrane bending de - ﬁnes a deformation in 3D where the area is not changed but where the membrane adopts a 30 Technical Description Of The Setup For Measuring Membrane Fission Rates A B C C A B A B C Figure 3 . 1 : Membrane deformations . A , Membrane stretching . B , Membrane bending . C , Membrane shearing . Source : Guillaume Molinard ( adapted ) , inspired by Evans and Needham ( 1987 ) . curved shape . Membrane shearing is the result of unisotropic forces that pull on the membrane without changing the area and lead to a re - arrangement of lipids . The elastic energy of a lipid membrane system can be described by the Canham - Helfrich Hamiltonian as a function of its shape ( Canham , 1970 ; Helfrich , 1973 ) : E el = σ ∆ A + (cid:90) A κ 2 J 2 d A ( 3 . 1 ) The energy contribution of membrane stretching is described by σ ∆ A . It is composed of the membrane tension σ , an elastic parameter which indicates to which degree the membrane is stretched , multiplied by the area diﬀerence due to stretching ∆ A . (cid:82) A κ 2 J 2 d A is the contribu - tion of membrane bending . κ is the membrane rigidity , a parameter that deﬁnes how energy consuming it is to bend the membrane and that depends on the lipid composition . The mean curvature J is deﬁned as : J = 1 R 1 + 1 R 2 ( 3 . 2 ) where R 1 and R 2 are the two principal radii that deﬁne a surface element ( Figure 3 . 2 ) . The integral takes into account all curvatures present in the given membrane system . As one can see , the Canham - Helfrich Hamiltonian does not include a term for the energy contribution of membrane shearing as it is negligible compared to the contributions of stretching and bending . Surface element Sphere Cylinder Saddle R 1 R 2 c 1 = 1 / R 1 c 2 = 1 / R 2 c 1 = c 2 = 1 / R J = 2 / R K = 1 / R 2 K = 0 J = 1 / R c 1 = 1 / R c 2 = 0 c 1 = - c 2 = 1 / R J = 0 K = - 1 / R 2 Figure 3 . 2 : Two principal radii of a surface element . Source : Guillaume Molinard , inspired by Kozlov et al . ( 2010 ) . 3 . 1 Basics Of Membrane Physics 31 3 . 1 . 2 Free Energy Of An Extruded Membrane Tube σ κ f L tube 2R tube Figure 3 . 3 : Nanotube extruded from an inﬁnite membrane reservoir with κ and σ . The Canham - Helfrich Hamiltonian can be calculated numerically in many cases , but only a few cases have simple analytical solutions . For example , calculating it for the 1D case of a membrane nanotube gives very simple solutions . Let us consider the free energy of a membrane nanotube that is extruded from an inﬁnite membrane reservoir ( Figure 3 . 3 ) . For a nanotube , the area expansion due to stretching ∆ A is equal to 2 π R tube L tube . The mean curvature J of a nanotube only depends on one radius ( R tube ) , because the other radius is parallel to the axis of the tube ( R 2 → ∞ ) , resulting in 1 R 2 → 0 . The product of f and L tube is added to the equation to include the force that is applied to hold the membrane tube . By replacing these values in the Canham - Helfrich Hamiltonian ( Equation 3 . 1 ) , we obtain the energy of the extruded nanotube ( Equation 3 . 3 ) : E el = 2 π R tube L tube ( σ + κ 2 R 2 tube ) − fL tube ( 3 . 3 ) Minimizing the energy of the membrane tube versus radius R tube results in Equation 3 . 4 : R tube 0 = (cid:114) κ 2 σ ( 3 . 4 ) The energy minimisation stems from the idea that one is interested in the radius of the tube at equilibrium which is reached very fast , depending on the membrane composition within a few seconds . R tube 0 describes the radius of the nanotube at equilibrium . Interestingly , R tube 0 is independent of the length of the nanotube , and only dependent on membrane rigidity κ and membrane tension σ . For membranes with high rigidity and low tension , tubes are wider . Low rigidity and high tension result in tubes that are more narrow . When minimising the free 32 Technical Description Of The Setup For Measuring Membrane Fission Rates energy of the membrane system for the length L tube and replacing R tube by (cid:112) κ 2 σ ( Equation 3 . 4 ) , Equation 3 . 5 for the force to hold the tube at equilibrium is obtained : f 0 = 2 π √ 2 κσ ( 3 . 5 ) The force at equilibrium will be high for high membrane rigidity and tension , and low for low membrane rigidity and tension . Equation 3 . 5 was experimentally veriﬁed by Evans et al . ( 1996 ) and Cuvelier et al . ( 2005 ) , using an experimental system similar to the nanotube pulling setup that I will present in the next section ( 3 . 2 ) . The experiments from Evans et al . ( 1996 ) and Cuvelier et al . ( 2005 ) were able to validate the force equation 3 . 5 , as the experimental results were in agreement with the predicted outcomes by this equation . 3 . 2 An Experimental System To Measure Membrane And Membrane Protein Properties This section introduces and explains the experimental setup that is used during this thesis for several purposes , namely measuring ﬁssion rates and eﬃciencies ( Chapter 4 ) , curvature inducing ( Section 3 . 2 . 4 ) and curvature sensing properties of proteins ( Chapter 5 ) . 3 . 2 . 1 Micropipette Aspiration To Control Membrane Tension Waugh and Evans ( 1979 ) introduced micropipette aspiration to study elastic properties of red blood cells . Two years later , the same technique was used to study elastic properties of giant unilamellar vesicles ( GUVs ) ( Kwok and Evans , 1981 ) . Aspiring a GUV with a micropipette leads to the formation of a membrane tongue inside the aspiration pipette due to the extra membrane area following membrane stretching ( Figure 3 . 4 ) . The membrane tension σ of the Aspiration pipette R pipette R GUV ∆ P GUV Figure 3 . 4 : Micropipette aspiration of a GUV . 3 . 2 An Experimental System To Measure Membrane And Membrane Protein Properties 33 GUV is set by the aspiration pressure ∆ P , the inner radius of the aspiration pipette R pipette and the radius of the GUV R GUV ( Equation 3 . 6 ) : σ = R pipette ∆ P 2 ( 1 − R pipette R GUV ) ( 3 . 6 ) This equation is obtained by applying the Young - Laplace equation ∆ P = 2 σ J twice , once for the interface of the GUV with the solution in the experimental chamber ( ∆ P chamb ) and once for the interface of the tongue with the liquid inside the pipette ( ∆ P tongue ) . Subtracting ∆ P chamb from ∆ P tongue leads to obtaining the total pressure diﬀerence ∆ P between the water reservoir of the aspiration pipette and the experimental chamber . Solving this new equation for σ gives Equation 3 . 6 . ∆ P can be controlled by connecting the micropipette to a tube that is ﬁlled with water and connected to a water reservoir that is displaceable in z . Changing the vertical position of the water reservoir by ∆ z results in a pressure diﬀerence ∆ P of : ∆ P = ρ water g ∆ z ( 3 . 7 ) with ρ water = 10 3 kgm 3 and g = 9 . 81 ms 2 . As we will see in Section 3 . 2 . 3 , these equations are used to calculate tension during membrane rigidity measurements . 3 . 2 . 2 The Nanotube Pulling Assay In Section 3 . 1 . 2 we have seen how the energy of a nanotube is described that was extruded from an inﬁnite membrane reservoir . The previous section ( 3 . 2 . 1 ) described a technique to set the membrane tension of a GUV by using an aspiration micropipette . Both concepts are combined in the nanotube pulling set up , where the GUV that is aspirated with an aspiration pipette is the membrane reservoir for the extrusion of a nanotube ( Figure 3 . 5 ) . Considering that the lipids that are part of the nanotube after extrusion are few compared to those that are part of the GUV , we can apply the force and membrane tension equations 3 . 4 and 3 . 5 from Section 3 . 1 . 2 . Due to the same approximation , a similar setup to the one presented in Figure 3 . 5 has been used to validate the force equation 3 . 5 ( Evans et al . , 1996 ; Cuvelier et al . , 2005 ) . Aspiration pipette Injection pipette Optical tweezers EndoDyn Figure 3 . 5 : Experimental setup of the nanotube pulling assay . 34 Technical Description Of The Setup For Measuring Membrane Fission Rates Figure 3 . 6 : Photography of the experimental chamber on top of an objective . Aspiration pipette ( lower left ) , two injection pipettes ( upper right ) . The experimental chamber is open on the sides for the micropipettes to enter . The liquid , typically 300 µ l , remains inside the chamber due to capillary action . In the nanotube pulling assay , the nanotube is extruded from a GUV by attaching a streptavidin - coated polystyrene bead to the GUV ( containing a small percentage of biotinylated lipids ) , on which we pull by means of optical tweezers . Optical tweezers consist of a focused laser beam . The resultant force of the forces applied by the photons when entering and existing the polystyrene bead push the bead towards the focal point of the laser beam . In our setup , the laser beam is focused via the objective of the microscope used for observation . The optical tweezers used for the nanotube pulling setup are on purpose adjusted to be weak , so that the force applied on the bead causes a visible shift in bead position that can be detected by brightﬁeld microscopy . Calibration of the optical tweezers by applying known forces and tracking the bead displacement indicates the stiﬀness of the optical tweezers . Stiﬀness deﬁnes which force is required to displace the bead by ∆ x . This then allows to determine the force that the tube applies on the bead based on the bead displacement . In addition , one or two injection pipettes are part of the setup ( Figure 3 . 5 , left ; Figure 3 . 6 , upper right ) with which proteins or any other components can be injected at the desired time point and for the desired duration . Each of the three micropipettes is connected to a diﬀerent water reservoir and a diﬀerent micromanipulator . The micromanipulators allow to move the pipettes in all three dimensions . 3 . 2 . 3 Membrane Rigidity Measurements The tube pulling setup can be used to measure membrane rigidity ( Cuvelier et al . , 2005 ) , employing the force equation 3 . 5 . For a given GUV , κ is constant , while membrane tension σ and force f are variable . Transcribing Equation 3 . 5 as f 2 = ( 8 π 2 κ ) σ ( 3 . 8 ) 3 . 2 An Experimental System To Measure Membrane And Membrane Protein Properties 35 0 50 100 150 200 0 500 1000 1500 2000 ∆σ , µN / m f 02 , p N 2 0 100 200 300 0 500 1000 1500 2000 σ , µN / m f 02 , p N 2 A B Figure 3 . 7 : Example of a membrane rigidity measurement , using a nanotube pulled from a GUV containing 99 % EPC , 1 % Rhodamine PE and 0 . 03 % biotinylated lipid . A , Plot of f 2 versus ∆ σ . B , Plot of f 2 versus σ . Slope : 5 . 8 ± 0 . 7 pN 2 µ N / m , κ = 17 . 5 ± 2 . 1 k B T . shows that σ is linearly proportional to f 2 . When experimentally varying the membrane tension of the GUV ( shown in Section 3 . 2 . 1 ) and recording ∆ z of the water reservoir displacement to calculate ∆ p ( Equation 3 . 7 ) and ∆ σ ( Equation 3 . 6 ) , and tracking the bead displacement to calculate the force f , then the slope of the plot of f 2 versus ∆ σ is equal to 8 π 2 κ . An example of such a plot is shown in Figure 3 . 7A . The linear ﬁt of the data points of the plot in Figure 3 . 7 to ax + b gives a slope of 5 . 8 ± 0 . 7 pN 2 µ N / m . As we can see , the ﬁt straight line does not go through ( 0 , 0 ) . This is due to the fact that we measured ∆ σ instead of absolute tension values , starting from an unknown starting tension of the GUV σ 0 . The negative x - intercept of the ﬁt straight line from the plot ( example in Figure 3 . 7 ) corresponds to this initial tension σ 0 . Adding σ 0 to the measured ∆ σ values gives the absolute tension σ . Plotting f 2 vs . σ results in 3 . 7B . Determining σ 0 is not needed for the calculation of the rigidity κ because the slope remains unchanged . In contrast , it is necessary for calculating the tube radius via Equations 3 . 4 and 3 . 9 , where the absolute membrane tension σ is required . 3 . 2 . 4 Measuring Curvature Sensing And Curvature Inducing Properties Of Proteins ( Incl . Summary Of Article 3 ) Apart from measuring membrane rigidity , the nanotube pulling setup can and has also been used to study properties of proteins that interact with the membrane . Sorre et al . ( 2012 ) used the technique to study curvature sensing and induction by the N - BAR protein amphiphysin . They injected amphiphysin on nanotubes in the tube pulling setup and measured the force before and during the injection of amphiphysin on the nanotube . By varying the aspiration before and during amphiphysin injection , they measured absolute tension in each case and could calculate the radius of the nanotube using Equation 3 . 9 , which is obtained by solving Equation 3 . 5 for κ and inserting it into Equation 3 . 4 : 36 Technical Description Of The Setup For Measuring Membrane Fission Rates R tube = f 4 πσ ( 3 . 9 ) They observed that amphiphysin preferentially bound to highly curved membranes , indepen - dently of the protein concentration . In contrast , amphiphysin did only induce curvature at intermediate to high bound protein densities . At intermediate bound densities , the force of the tube on the bead decreased upon amphiphysin binding , but the radius of the tube was still dependent on membrane tension . At high bound densities , the tube radius was independent of membrane tension but was instead set by the amphiphysin scaﬀold . At very low protein concentrations ( dilute limit ) , amphiphysin did not induce but only sensed curvature . During my thesis , I used the same approach to test curvature inducing properties of the clathrin adapter AP180 for a collaboration with my former lab colleague Mohammed Saleem . He studied clathrin polymerisation and observed that clathrin deformed GUVs when their membrane tension was low , but not when membrane tension was high ( Article 3 , Saleem et al . ( 2015 ) ) . As clathrin needs adapters to bind to the membrane , he used the clathrin adapter AP180 . Testing curvature deforming properties of AP180 was important in order to assign the observed phenotype either to clathrin alone , AP180 alone or to a combination of AP180 and clathrin . I injected AP180 on nanotubes in the tube pulling assay and measured the force before and during injection of AP180 . The force remained unchanged ( Figure 3 . 8 ) . This showed that clathrin was responsible , in combination with AP180 , for the membrane deformation and not AP180 alone . The paper “A balance between membrane elasticity and polymerization energy sets the shape of spherical clathrin coats” ( Article 3 , Saleem et al . ( 2015 ) ) to which I contributed can be found in the Appendix of this thesis . In summary , using in vitro reconstitution of clathrin polymerisation , followed by either EM or ﬂuorescence microscopy . two diﬀerent types of membrane deformations were observed , either shallow pits at moderate membrane tension or deep buds at low membrane tension . Also high membrane rigidity was opposing clathrin polymerisation . A theoretical model was developped to describe the competition between the energy loss to deform the membrane ( depending on membrane elastic parameters κ and σ ) , the energy gain by polymerisation of clathrin triskelia and the energy loss due to triskelia arms that are not bound to other triskelia before injection during injection 0 20 40 60 Fo r ce ( p N ) n . s . Figure 3 . 8 : AP180 did not induce a force drop when injected on nanotubes . Adapted from Saleem et al . ( 2015 ) . A new ﬁgure from the force data set was made as there was an unnoticed technical problem when the publisher of the paper generated the ﬁnal pdf . Error bars , standard deviation . 3 . 2 An Experimental System To Measure Membrane And Membrane Protein Properties 37 arms ( line tension ) . Clathrin would only polymerise on the membrane if the energy gain due to polymerization is higher than the energy loss due to membrane bending , stretching and increased line tension . Mathematical calculations and experimental measurements allowed to give an estimate of the binding energy of 23 ± 3 k B T per triskelion . Roux et al . ( 2010 ) used the tube pulling technique to measure curvature - dependent dynamin polymerisation and to determine the concentration range in solution at which dynamin poly - merises in a curvature - dependent manner , as well as the curvature range in which dynamin nucleates at all . The tube pulling setup was also used by Prévost et al . ( 2015 ) to measure sensing and induction of negative curvature by the I - BAR ( inverted BAR , see also Section 2 . 2 . 1 ) protein IRSp53 . In contrast to the procedure that I used , the I - BAR protein was encapsulated into the GUV because I - BAR proteins sense negative and not positive curvature . Recently , the tube pulling assay was employed by Simunovic et al . ( 2016 ) , together with other approaches , to analyse how BAR proteins form a scaﬀold on membrane tubes and found that the amphipathic helices of the BAR domain are not required for scaﬀold formation . Simulations suggested that a rigid scaﬀold was already possible to be obtained as of a membrane coverage by the protein of only 30 – 40 % . Chen et al . ( 2016 ) , using among other techniques the tube pulling assay , came to the conclusion that amphipathic helices are not required for curvature sensing but do contribute to curvature sensing when the curvature is high ( r < 40 nm ) . 3 . 2 . 5 Measuring Dynamin - Mediated Membrane Fission Rates Another application of the nanotube pulling assay is to study membrane ﬁssion ( Morlot et al . , 2012 ) . In this study , a nanotube was pulled from a GUV and dynamin + GTP were injected . They deﬁned the ﬁssion time as the time between the appearance of the ﬁrst nucleation spot of dynamin on the tube and the moment that the tube was cut . They discovered that membrane ﬁssion was a stochastic process , in which not membrane constriction of dynamin on its own induced ﬁssion , but instead occured at a time point after constriction . As the process was stochastic , the probability p t that a tube had been cut until the time point t increased over time and converged to 100 % . The obtained data points were ﬁt to 1 − e − t τ , allowing to obtain the characteristic time τ until which half the tubes underwent ﬁssion in each condition . Fission occured in most cases either close to the bead or close to the GUV and only rarely in the middle of the tube . By increasing time resolution , ﬁssion was observed to take place at the border of dynamin polymers ( Figure 3 . 9 ) . While tension reduced the ﬁssion time , membrane rigidity was delaying ﬁssion . Low membrane tension also reduced ﬁssion in living cells . These ﬁndings were in agreement with a model in which membrane elastic parameters inﬂuence ﬁssion because ﬁssion occurs at the interface between a dynamin - constricted membrane tube and the bare membrane . Dynamin - mediated constriction reduces the energy barrier at this interface , so that ﬁssion then occurs spontaneously due to thermal ﬂuctuations of the membrane , leading to the hemiﬁssion state . These ﬁndings were essential for proposing the constriction model which is currently one of the two models at debate to explain dynamin - mediated membrane ﬁssion ( see Section 2 . 1 . 4 ) . 38 Technical Description Of The Setup For Measuring Membrane Fission Rates ‘‘dynamin - membrane edge’’ ) . By setting the constriction radius R c , s , and k ( see Extended Experimental Procedures ) and numerically minimizing the elastic energy of the membrane , we can calculate the shape of the dynamin - membrane edge ( Fig - ures 1F and 1G ) . The funnel shape of the dynamin - membrane edge is associated with a local increase in elastic energy that can be estimated numerically ( Figure 2B ) ( Shlomovitz et al . , 2011 ) . This elastic energy depends on the ratio a = R m / R c , where Figure 1 . Localization of Fission Events at Dynamin - Membrane Edges ( A ) Schematic drawing of the experimental set - up . A second micropipette ( left ) injects locally dynamin and GTP . After ﬁssion , extremity of the left stump is covered with green dynamin , whereas the right stump is uncoated , showing that ﬁssion occurred at the edge between a seed of dynamin ( white arrows ) and the dynamin - free membrane nanotube ( see also Figure S1 and Movie S2 ) . ( F ) Fluorescence image of a membrane tube constricted by dynamin in presence of GTP ( TMR - PE ) . Scale bars , 5 m m . ( G ) Calculated shape a single dynamin - membrane edge by simulations . R m is the radius of the bare tube , which is set by membrane tension and bend - ing rigidity . Thus , the smaller R c is ( the more dynamin constricts ) , the higher the elastic energy of the dynamin - membrane edge is . We reasoned that the local increase of elastic energy of the membrane edge could favor ﬁssion by reducing its energy barrier . Fission was proposed to occur wherever the membrane reaches a hemi - ﬁssion state , when the membrane radius shrinks below a threshold R i (cid:31) 3 nm ( Ko - zlovsky and Kozlov , 2003 ) , comparable to the membrane thick - ness ( see ﬁssion intermediate in Figure 2A ) . The existence of such hemiﬁssion intermediate is supported by the experimental fact that ﬁssion is nonleaky ( Bashkirov et al . , 2008 ) . Reaching an intermediate state with such a strongly curved membrane is a rare event and must thus be the rate - limiting step of membrane Cell 151 , 619 – 629 , October 26 , 2012 ª 2012 Elsevier Inc . 621 Figure 3 . 9 : Fission occured at the border of dynamin polymers ( green ) . Red , membrane channel . Scale bar , 5 µ m . Source : Morlot et al . ( 2012 ) . Chapter 4 Thesis Work : Endophilin Inhibits Dynamin - Mediated Fission Contents 4 . 1 Introduction To Article 2 . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . 39 4 . 2 Article 2 : The endophilin - dynamin co - complex inhibits membrane ﬁssion . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . 40 4 . 3 Summary Of Article 2 . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . 71 4 . 4 Complementary Experiments . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . 71 4 . 4 . 1 Injection Of Endophilin On Pre - Formed Dynamin Polymers . . . . . 71 4 . 4 . 2 Assessment Of Fission Inhibition Of Endophilin Without Binding To The Membrane . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . 73 4 . 4 . 3 Cloning Of An Endophilin - Dynamin Chimera Plasmid . . . . . . . . 74 4 . 4 . 4 Endophilin - Dynamin Chimera Expression In Mammalian Cells . . . . 75 4 . 4 . 5 Transferrin Uptake In Mammalian Cells Expressing An Endophilin - Dynamin Chimera . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . . 76 4 . 1 Introduction To Article 2 In the previous chapters we have seen that dynamin mediates membrane ﬁssion , via constricting the underlying membrane tube after several cycles of GTP binding , binding to the GTPase domain of the adjacent helix turn , GTP hydrolysis , power stroke , release and restart of the cycle ( Antonny et al . , 2016 ) . Following constriction , spontaneous ﬁssion of the membrane occurs due to thermal ﬂuctuations ( Morlot et al . , 2012 ) . We have also seen that BAR proteins directly interact with dynamin and the membrane and that dynamin was proposed to be recruited to vesicle necks by endophilin ( Sundborger et al . , 2011 ) . However , it is still under debate whether and how BAR and especially N - BAR proteins regulate ﬁssion itself . While endophilin was initially proposed to inhibit ﬁssion ( Farsad et al . , 2001 ) , recent results suggested the opposite ( Meinecke et al . , 2013 ; Neumann and Schmid , 2013 ) . In order to obtain clarity on this matter , we decided to measure ﬁssion rates and eﬃciencies for the endophilin - dynamin co - complex and employed electron microscopy to visualise its structure . 40 Thesis Work : Endophilin Inhibits Dynamin - Mediated Fission A summary of the article is presented in Section 4 . 3 . 4 . 2 Article 2 : The endophilin - dynamin co - complex inhibits membrane ﬁssion Manuscript in preparation . Authors : Annika Hohendahl , Nathaniel Talledge , Frédéric Humbert , Valentina Galli , Adam Frost , Aurélien Roux . 1 Structural inhibition of dynamin - mediated membrane fission by endophilin Annika Hohendahl 1 , Nathaniel Talledge 2 , Frédéric Humbert 1 , Valentina Galli 1 , Adam Frost 2 , Aurélien Roux 1 , 3 1 Biochemistry Department , University of Geneva , 1211 Geneva , Switzerland . 2 Department of Biochemistry & Biophysics , UCSF , San Francisco , CA 94143 , USA . 3 Swiss National Centre for Competence in Research Programme Chemical Biology , 1211 Geneva , Switzerland . INTRODUCTION Dynamin is a 97kDa GTPase that mediates membrane fission in several endocytic routes . Dynamin forms tetramers in solution via the stalk domain ( Muhlberg et al . , 1997 ; Reubold et al . , 2015 ) and helical polymers around membrane tubes ( Sweitzer and Hinshaw , 1998 ) . In these polymers , the GTPase ( G ) domains of adjacent dynamin helix rungs interact , increasing dynamin ' s GTPase activity 1000 fold ( Stowell et al . , 1999 ) . Constriction of the dynamin helix is required for membrane fission ( Antonny et al . , 2016 ) , but how the GTPase activity is coupled to constriction is still debated . The disassembly model proposes that dynamin assembles into a highly constricted helix in the GTP - loaded state , and that GTP - hydrolysis dependent disassembly promotes fission ( Shnyrova et al . , 2013 ) . In the constriction / ratchet model , dynamin GTPase domains are proposed to act as motor heads that use GTP hydrolysis to drive relative displacement of helical turns and thereby decrease the dynamin helix perimeter to constrict the underlying membrane tube . Spontaneous fission then takes place at the edge of the constricted tube due to thermal fluctuations ( Morlot et al . , 2012 ) . 2 In the cell , dynamin is recruited to endocytic vesicle necks just before fission ( Taylor et al . , 2011 ) . The dynamin - binding N - BAR proteins are proposed to participate in this recruitment ( Ferguson and De Camilli , 2012 ; Taylor et al . , 2011 ) . N - BAR proteins are a subfamily of the crescent - shaped BIN1 / Amphiphysin / Rvs167 ( BAR ) proteins ( Peter et al . , 2004 ) with an additional N - terminal amphipathic helix . N - BAR proteins sense and induce membrane curvature ( Farsad et al . , 2001 ; Mim et al . , 2012 ; Sorre et al . , 2012 ; Takei et al . , 1999 ) , and are thus proposed to either induce or bind avidly to the highly curved necks of endocytic pits . The SH3 domain of N - BAR binds to dynamin ' s proline - rich domain ( PRD ) ( Grabs et al . , 1997 ; Ringstad et al . , 1997 ) recruiting dynamin to vesicle necks ( Sundborger et al . , 2011 ) . However , the role of N - BAR proteins in membrane fission is still unclear . The N - terminal alpha - helix induces membrane curvature , and thus promotes constriction and possibly fission ( Boucrot et al . , 2012 ) . On the other hand , the BAR domain is proposed to act as a stable scaffold , blocking further constriction below its preferred curvature and thereby inhibiting fission ( Boucrot et al . , 2012 ) . The role of N - BAR proteins in dynamin - mediated membrane fission is even more unclear : amphiphysin was proposed to enhance dynamin - mediated membrane fission ( Takei et al . , 1999 ) , a stimulatory effect found to be curvature - dependent later ( Yoshida et al . , 2004 ) . Early findings showed that endophilin inhibited dynamin - mediated membrane fission ( Farsad et al . , 2001 ) . However , different results were obtained in other assays ( Meinecke et al . , 2013 ; Neumann and Schmid , 2013 ) . In some cases , N - BAR proteins were found to inhibit the GTPase activity of dynamin , but still stimulated its fission reaction ( Neumann and Schmid , 2013 ) . Because of the large variability of published results , we ought to test the effect of the endophilin / dynamin interaction onto the fission rate of dynamin . We employed different membrane templates to measure fission rates and efficiencies of the endophilin - dynamin co - complex and EM to visualise the structures of the co - complex . 3 MATERIALS AND METHODS Materials Guanosine 5′ - triphosphate ( GTP , 10106399001 ) was purchased from Roche Diagnostics GmBH , Mannheim , Germany . Streptavidin - coated beads ( SVP - 30 - 5 ) were purchased from Spherotech , Lake Forest , USA . 4 Dynamin purification Human dynamin 1 was purified from baculovirus - infected Sf9 cells expressing recombinant dynamin 1 , via affinity purification with the SH3 domain of rat amphiphysin 1 ( Stowell et al . , 1999 ) . Typically , 2 l of Sf9 cells were infected with recombinant baculovirus and incubated under agitation for 3 days . The cell lysate was resuspended in 50 ml of buffer A ( 20 mM HEPES , 100 mM NaCl , 1 mM EGTA , 1 mM DTT , pH 7 . 4 ) + protease inhibitor tablets ( cOmplete EDTA - free Protease Inhibitor Cocktail , 05056489001 , Roche Diagnostics GmbH , Mannheim , Germany ) . After homogenisation and centrifugation , the supernatant was incubated under agitation for 2 h at 4 °C with 5 ml glutathione Sepharose beads ( Glutathione Sepharose 4B , 17 - 0756 - 05 , GE Healthcare Bio - Sciences AB , Uppsala , Sweden ) to which 10 mg of GST - tagged amphiphysin 1 - SH3 domain had been attached . After three washes with buffer A , the bead suspension was loaded into a column and the protein eluted with high salt buffer B ( 20 mM PIPES , 1 . 2 M NaCl , 1 mM DTT , pH 6 . 5 ) . The protein positive fractions were pooled , dialysed against GTPase buffer ( 20 mM HEPES , 100 mM NaCl , 1 mM MgCl 2 , pH 7 . 4 ) and concentrated on an Amicon 50 kDa column ( Merck Millipore Ltd . , Carrigtwohill , Ireland ) . Purification of endophilin constructs Rat endophilin A1 was produced from a pGEX - 6P vector in E . coli upon induction with IPTG for 3 h at 37 °C . The pellet was resuspended in PBS + 1 % Triton X - 100 + cOmplete protease inhibitor tablets ( see above ) . The 50 ml supernatant after sonication and centrifugation was incubated for 1 h at 4 °C with 7 . 5 ml glutathione Sepharose beads ( ABT , Miami , USA ) . Following two washes with cleavage buffer ( 50 mM Tris , 150 mM NaCl , 1 mM EDTA , 1 mM DTT , pH 7 . 5 ) , PreScission enzyme was added to cut off the endophilin from 5 the column , while the GST tag remains attached . The incubation was over night at 4 °C with agitation . Protein positive fractions of the flow through were pooled , concentrated on a Vivaspin 6 10 kDa column ( Sartorius Stedim Biotech GmbH , Göttingen , Germany ) and dialysed against GTPase buffer . The plasmids for the SH3 and BAR domains of endophilin were a kind gift of Pietro De Camilli ( Yale University ) . The BAR domain was purified like full - length endophilin , apart from the PreScission treatment which was done in solution , prior to adding the suspension to a column . The SH3 domain was purified similarly to full - length endophilin , but with the following differences : the protein production with IPTG was performed only during 2 h ; the SH3 domain was eluted from the beads on a column by addition of glutathione ; only then the GST - tag was cut off from the SH3 domain by PreScission treatment ; a second incubation with glutathione Sepharose beads followed to remove free GST and PreScission which also contained a GST - tag . Protein labelling Fluorescent dynamin was obtained by labelling with Atto 488 iodoacetamide ( AD 488 - 111 , ATTO - TEC GmbH , Siegen , Germany ) at a molar ratio of 1 : 3 ( protein vs . label ) , following the manufacturer ' s labelling protocol . Half fluorescently labelled and half non - labelled dynamin was used in fluorescence microscopy . Endophilin and endophilin ' s BAR domain were labelled with Atto 390 NHS - ester ( AD 390 - 31 , see above ) at a molar ratio of 1 : 3 . In some cases , endophilin was labelled with Atto 390 iodoacetamide ( AD 390 - 111 ) or Atto 565 iodoacetamide ( AD 565 - 111 ; membrane sheets colocalisation ) . 6 Vesicle preparation Three different membrane compositions were used for unilamellar vesicles ( GUVs ) in the tube - pulling experiments , each of these supplemented with 0 . 03 % DSPE - PEG ( 2000 ) Biotin to allow binding to the streptavidin - coated bead : 28 . 5 % DOPC , 28 . 5 % DOPE , 20 % DOPS , 9 % Brain PIP 2 , 13 % cholesterol , 1 % TMR - PIP 2 ( 3321 , Fig . 2 ) ; 80 % EPC + 19 % PIP 2 + 1 % TMR - PIP 2 ( 80 : 20 , Fig . 3 ) ; 29 % DOPC , 29 % DOPE , 11 % DOPS , 17 % Brain PIP 2 , 13 % cholesterol , 1 % TMR - PIP 2 ( 3312 , Fig . 4 ) . Percentages are mole percentages . For preparing GUVs , 10 - 15 µl lipid mix of 1 - 2 g / l lipids in pure chloroform were deposited on 2 indium tin oxide ( ITO ) coated slides and dried for 1 h at 55 °C . A chamber was assembled with a teflon O - ring between the two slides and it was filled with ~ 400 µl sucrose of 200 - 230 mOsm ( adjusted ± 1 mOsm to the respective experimental buffer ) . The GUVs were electroformed by applying sinus voltage of 1 V at 10 Hz for 1 h at 55 °C . SUVs for electron microscopy ( EM ) were prepared by premixing lipid stocks stored in chloroform into the correct molar ratios . The mixtures were then placed into a 5 mL reaction vial ( TS - 13223 , Thermo Fisher Scientific , Waltham , MA USA ) and the lipids were dried onto the glass surface by vortexing over a stream of Nitrogen gas . Lipids were then reconstituted in 0 . 2 mL Hexane , followed by the same vortex drying procedure , to obtain an evenly dried lipid coat on the reaction vial . The samples were lyophilized for > 1 hour to remove any residual solvent . Lipid mixtures were then reconstituted in GTPase buffer to make a final SUV solution of 1 mg / mL . The sample mixed 12 - 16 hours in a tube rotator to fully reconstitute the lipids from the side of the glass reaction vial . The samples were then subjected to 5 freeze thaw cycles to burst any multi - lamellar liposomes . SUV compositions were either 28 % DOPC , 28 % DOPE , 11 % DOPS , 17 % PIP 2 , 15 % cholesterol or 80 % DOPC , 20 % PIP 2 ( molar % ) . 7 SUVs for the GTPase assay were made by drying 200 µl 10 g / l chloroform solution of 95 % BPL and 5 % Brain PIP 2 in a glass vial with a nitrogen flow . The lipids were rehydrated in 1 ml GTPase buffer and incubated at 37 °C for 1 h , followed by vortexing and sonication . Membrane sheets assay A lipid solution of 10 mg / ml containing 26 % Brain PE , 4 . 5 % Liver PI , 26 % POPS , 30 . 5 % POPC and 13 % cholesterol was prepared , which was then supplemented with 5 % final Brain PIP 2 . Glass cover slips were cleaned with chloroform . Droplets of 1 . 5 μl of above lipid solution were deposited on the cover slip , allowed to dry , and then dried in the vacuum oven for at least one hour . A chamber of ~ 25µl was built by placing the coverslip onto a glass slide , the dried lipid drops facing the glass slide , using a double - sided Scotch ( 3M ) tape as a spacer ( see Fig . 2 in Itoh et al . ( 2005 ) ) . The lipids were fully re - hydrated by injecting 25 μl of 4 g / l casein in GTPase buffer . Rehydration generated membrane sheets , as previously described ( Suzuki and Masuhara , 2005 ) . The glass slide was placed on the stage of either an Axiovert 200 ZEISS ( Germany ) microscope for observation with a JAI Pulnix ( USA ) TM1400CL camera and DVR software ( Advanced Digital Vision Inc . USA ) , or an inverted spinning disk confocal microscope ( Nikon Eclipse T1 with spinning disk from 3I , Denver , CO , USA ) with a 100x oil objective ( Nikon CFI Apo TIRF 100x NA 1 . 4 ) . To generate tubules coated with both endophilin and dynamin , endophilin was added to the chamber with a molar excess of at least 4 times compared to dynamin ( typically 16 µM ) . Then , 5 μl of a dynamin containing solution ( typically 4 µM ) were applied to one side of the chamber and the deformation of membrane sheets produced by its diffusion into the chamber under Differential Interference Contrast ( DIC ) settings . 5 μl of 1 mM GTP containing buffer were added after formation of the tubules . 8 For experiments involving COOH - coated beads ( negatively charged at neutral pH , 320 nm diameter , Bangs Labs , USA ) , beads were diluted 500 - 1000 fold in the dynamin solution prior to injection . Only tubules not adherent to the glass surface throughout their length were selected for observation . Bead rotation analysis For the analysis of the bead movement , movies were contrasted using virtualdub , transformed to 8 bit grayscale stack ( . stk ) files using the ImageJ software , and the spinning beads were tracked using the Tracking Function of the Metamorph software ( Molecular Devices Corp . , USA ) . For each tubule type , the average maximal angular speed was calculated from the maximal speeds ( which in turn was an average of at least three turns ) of 15 to 30 beads . Tube pulling assay A ~ 2 mm high chamber was assembled between two rectangular horizontal glass slides and mounted on the stage of an inverted scanning confocal microscope ( Eclipse T1 with A1R scanner , Nikon , Tokyo , Japan ) with a 100x oil objective ( CFI Plan Apo VC 100X Oil NA 1 . 4 , Nikon , see above ) . The microscopy setup included home - made optical tweezers , for which an ytterbium fibre laser ( IPG Photonics , Oxford , USA ) was focussed through the microscopy objective . The chamber was pre - treated with 4 g / l casein in GTPase buffer and then filled by capillarity with a mixture of GTPase buffer and ( 0 . 02 % ( v / v ) ) streptavidin coated beads of 3 . 05 µm average diameter . A GUV was aspirated by a glass pipette ( Fig . 2A ) which was controlled by a micromanipulator ( MP - 225 , Sutter Instrument , Novato , USA ) . A streptavidin coated bead was hold by the optical tweezers , and a nanotube pulled from this bead by first touching it with the GUV and then pulling the GUV away . Time - lapse imaging was started 9 and the protein ( s ) in GTPase buffer , in some cases together with GTP , injected with a second micropipette that was controlled by a manual micromanipulator ( Narishige , Tokyo , Japan ) . In some experiments , a third micropipette was used for injection of a different protein mixture , controlled by a third micromanipulator ( MP - 285 , Sutter , see above ) . GTPase assay We used the malachite green assay to monitor the release of inorganic phosphate due to the GTPase activity of dynamin ( Quan and Robinson , 2005 ) . GTPase activity was measured in the presence of SUVs containing 95 % BPL and 5 % Brain PIP 2 ( see Vesicle Preparation for details on preparation ) . All mixes were performed on the same 96 - well plate , and a molar ratio of approximately four between endophilin and dynamin was used . The assay was performed in a total reaction volume of 50 µl , containing typically 200 nM dynamin ( plus eventually 800 nM endophilin ) , 2 µl SUVs and 100 µM GTP . The buffer of the reaction was GTPase buffer . Incubation prior to addition of malachite working solution was for 30 min at 37 °C . Image analysis Image analysis was performed with ImageJ . Matlab was used to make fits . Membrane remodelling reactions for electron microscopy Purified protein reagents and unilamellar liposomes were mixed together and allowed to incubate at room temperature for 30 minutes . To generate the homo or hetero polymers of dynamin and endophilin , protein was added to a final concentration of 4 µM mixed with the appropriate nucleotide to a final concentration of 1 mM . Reaction buffer was GTPase buffer . The protein to lipid ratio was 1 : 2 by mass . Remodelled membranes in many cases could be 10 observed by TEM within 5 min of the assembly reaction and were observed at protein concentrations as low as 0 . 5 µM . Negative stain electron microscopy Protein remodelled membranes were prepared for TEM following established procedures ( Booth et al . , 2011 ) . Continuous carbon grids ( 400 mesh copper ) were prepared by glow - discharging the surface ( PELCO EasiGlow , 15 mA , 0 . 39 mBar , 30 seconds ) . Each sample ( 5 µL ) was allowed to absorb onto the grid surface for 2 min followed by blotting onto filter paper . The grids were then stained with 0 . 75 % ( w / v ) uranyl formate for 30 sec , blotted , and allowed to air dry . Samples were imaged with a Tecnai T12 microscope ( FEI ) equipped with a LaB6 filament and operated at 120 kV and data captured with a Gatan Ultrascan CCD camera ( Gatan ) . Cryogenic Electron microscopy Membrane remodelled protein reactions were applied to a glow - discharged ( PELCO EasiGlow , 15 mA , 0 . 39 mBar , 30 seconds ) Quantifoil holey carbon grid ( 2 µm holes , 2 µm spacing , 200 mesh ) in a Vitrobot Mark III ( FEI ) . Specifically , 3 . 5 µL of sample was applied in a 100 % humidity 19 °C chamber , allowed to absorb to the grid surface for 30 sec , blotted against filter paper for 1 . 5 - 4 . 5 sec ( 0 mm offset ) , and then plunge frozen into liquid ethane . Samples were stored in liquid nitrogen until imaging could take place ( Grassucci et al . , 2007 ) . Electron cryo - micrographs were collected using standard low - dose procedures 11 RESULTS Endophilin inhibits dynamin - mediated fission ( FIGURE 1 ) In order to study the effect of endophilin on dynamin - mediated fission , lipid tubules were generated from hydrated membrane sheets with these proteins ( see Methods ) . As membrane sheets are a low tension membrane reservoir , curvature - inducing proteins ( such as dynamin and endophilin ) deform them into tubular structures ( Itoh et al . , 2005 ; Roux et al . , 2006 ) . Once formed , membrane sheets were thus incubated either with dynamin alone ( Fig . 1A ) or sequentially with first endophilin and then dynamin ( Fig . 1B ) . The endophilin - dynamin tubules looked thicker and more contrasted under Differential Interference Contrast ( DIC ) microscopy , probably reflecting the co - assembly of endophilin and dynamin . Indeed , by using fluorescently labelled proteins ( see Fig . 1D ) , we observed that these proteins where co - assembled onto the tubules . GTP was then added ( t = 0 sec ) and videos of the dynamin and endophilin - dynamin tubules were recorded . While the dynamin tubules underwent fission within a few seconds , the endophilin - dynamin tubules did not break . We concluded from these experiment that endophilin was inhibiting dynamin - mediated membrane fission . To further investigate this inhibiting function , we tested dynamin activity in the presence of endophilin in several functional assays . As previously reported ( Farsad et al . , 2001 ) , dynamin ' s GTPase activity was decreased in the presence of endophilin , as measured by malachite green assay ( Fig . 1C ) . We further tested if dynamin still underwent GTP hydrolysis - driven mechano - chemical constriction in the presence of endophilin by visualizing the rotation of beads attached to dynamin - coated lipid tubules after addition of GTP into the chamber ( Roux et al . , 2006 ) . As previously shown , beads rotated with an average speed of 8 - 9 rotations / second when dynamin alone was used , whereas no rotation 12 was observed in the presence of endophilin ( Fig . 1E , F ) . These results suggested that endophilin blocked dynamin constriction – thereby reducing its GTPase activity – and inhibiting membrane fission . Endophilin reduces fission rate and efficiency in a concentration - dependent manner ( FIGURE 2 ) To better characterize and define the required molecular interactions for this fission inhibition , we used an assay that enabled us to measure the rate of dynamin - mediated membrane fission ( Fig . 2A ) . A giant unilamellar vesicle ( GUV ) was held under aspiration into a glass micropipette , and a lipid nanotube was pulled out from the GUV by means of optical tweezers ( Methods and Morlot et al . , 2012 ) . Dynamin , endophilin and GTP were injected in the proximity of the membrane tube via separate injection pipettes allowing for various sequences of injection during time - lapse confocal imaging . The fission time – which is the inverse of the fission rate – was defined as the time between the start of the injection and the breakage of the tube ( Fig . 2C ) . We measured fission times and plotted cumulative probability curves for various endophilin / dynamin molar concentration ratios , with a constant concentration of dynamin of 5 µM . Exponential fits to a * ( 1 - exp ( - t / τ ) ) ( Matlab ) revealed the fission efficiency ( a ) and characteristic time ( τ ) for each condition , incl . 95 % confidence intervals for the two fit parameters . Fission efficiency a corresponds to the percentage of tubes that are not cut . At low ratios ( 0 . 5x / 1x ) , fission still took place in most cases , but was delayed ( 39 . 5 ± 3 . 8 sec and 52 . 8 ± 7 . 8 sec , respectively , compared to 15 . 8 ± 3 . 7 sec for dynamin alone ; Fig . 2E , F , G ) . At high endophilin ratios ( 4x ) , where both dynamin and endophilin clearly bound to the tube ( Fig . 2D ) , fission was completely inhibited ( Fig . 2E , F , G ) . 13 To test whether direct interactions between dynamin and endophilin , and endophilin and the membrane were required for this inhibition , we tested the effect of endophilin ' s BAR and SH3 domains on dynamin fission rates and efficiency at the highest ( 4x ) concentration ratio ( Fig . 2B ) . No difference in fission efficiency was observed for the SH3 domain ( Fig . 2H , I ) . By contrast , the BAR domain alone , a known curvature inducer ( Farsad et al . , 2001 ) , significantly decreased the fission rate ( Fig . 2H , J ) , while fission efficiency was only slightly reduced ( Fig . 2H , I ) by comparison with full length endophilin ( 4x ) ( Fig . 2H , I ) . As changing the endophilin / dynamin ratio affects the total protein concentration in solution , we wondered how the inhibitory effect of endophilin was affected by the total protein concentration . Instead of keeping the dynamin concentration constant , we measured fission times for solutions where the total protein concentration was kept constant at 5 µM , adjusting the dynamin and endophilin concentrations according to the required final ratio . In this case , the inhibitory effect was also present , even though slightly less pronounced than when the dynamin concentration was kept constant at 5 µM ( Fig . 2H , I , J ) . As changing the concentrations of dynamin and endophilin affects their ability to bind on these membrane tubules ( Roux et al . , 2010 ; Sorre et al . , 2012 ) , these experiments may not reach the exact same endophilin / dynamin ratio on the tube than for experiments where dynamin concentration was kept constant . Endophilin is binding to membrane between dynamin rings and dynamin is further apart in copolymer We next wondered by which mechanism endophilin inhibited dynamin ' s fission activity . One possibility would be the observed downregulation of the GTPase activity of dynamin by endophilin ( Yoshida et al . ( 2004 ) ; Fig . 1C ) . At the same time , the distance between turns of dynamin is increased by a factor of 2 in the presence of endophilin , as seen by electron 14 microscopy ( EM ) ( Farsad et al . , 2001 ) . We thus hypothesised that the change in the coat structure might be due to the intercalation of endophilin between the dynamin rings , blocking molecular interactions between GTPase domains that are thought to be responsible for enhanced GTPase activity and constriction . However , currently available EM images do not have enough resolution to distinguish BAR domain proteins in between the turns of the dynamin helix . We thus prepared samples for cryo - EM , hoping that the higher resolution would resolve the relevant molecular interactions . . Dynamin alone , endophilin alone or various mixtures were incubated with liposomes . As previously reported ( Farsad et al . , 2001 ) , apparent turns of Dynamin were space further apart in the co - complex than in the sample with dynamin alone ( Fig . 3A ) . Asymmetric units of the co - complex from cryo - EM micrographs were extracted for further analysis by classification and class averaging ( Supplemental Figure 1A ) . In those images projected perpendicularly to the axis of the BAR domain , endophilin appeared as a triangular shape bound to the membrane tube ( see Fig . 3B ) . Dynamin appeared as a T - shaped structure , consistent with previous images in which the tips of the T - shape correspond with the GTPase domains and the body of the T - shape corresponds with the dimeric stalk ( Chappie et al . , 2010 ; Zhang and Hinshaw , 2001 ) . In the co - complex , raw micrographs and class averages show that endophilin molecules are intercalated in between the dynamin rings ( Fig . 3B ) , clearly separating the GTPase domains . Most of the asymmetric units were found to belong to one of two classes with either 2 or 3 endophilin molecules separating turns of dynamin ( Fig . 2E ) . As there are about 28 monomers of dynamin per helical turn ( Chen et al . , 2004 ; Zhang and Hinshaw , 2001 ) , and between 8 - 16 monomers of endophilin ( Mim et al . , 2012 ) , dynamin could recruit enough endophilin to form up to 2 - 3 turns . From these results we concluded that when endophilin and dynamin are both bound to the membrane and to each other through their PRD - SH3 domains , endophilin is inserted 15 between turns of a dynamin oligomer . In this arrangement , the dynamin molecules from adjacent turns are sufficiently far apart that they are unable to interact , inhibiting G domain dimerization and GTP hydrolysis - driven constriction Endophilin reduces dynamin signal on tube , correlating with fission inhibition ( FIGURE 4 ) Following the observations that endophilin was inhibitory for fission ( Fig . 1 , 2 ) and that it inserted in between the turns of the dynamin helix ( Fig . 3B ) , we hypothesized that the insertion and alternated coat architecture was responsible for fission inhibition . To test this hypothesis , we looked for a way to monitor fission rate as a function of dynamin density on the tube , assuming that a reduction of the dynamin density would reflect insertion of endophilin within the dynamin coat . Thus , we used the tube pulling assay , and tubes were decorated by co - injection of dynamin and endophilin ( Fig . 4A ) . The formation of the co - complex was assessed by measuring the fluorescence signals of both proteins , and then GTP was injected onto the same tube to measure the fission time . The dynamin signal was clearly lower when endophilin was co - injected , as compared to dynamin alone ( Fig . 4B , C , D ) , showing that endophilin was intercalating within the dynamin coat . The endophilin signal on the tube was , as expected , increasing with increasing endophilin concentrations in solution ( Fig . 4E ) . The lower dynamin fluorescence was in agreement with the changes in dynamin density in the co - polymer observed by EM ( Fig . 3B ) . Fission activity was dramatically reduced on tubes with the endophilin - dynamin co - complex , whereas it proceeded normally on tubes coated with dynamin only ( Fig . 4F ) . Our results thus support that the endophilin intercalation directly caused the fission inhibition . 16 DISCUSSION In this study , we have tested the effect of endophilin on dynamin ' s membrane fission activity . Our results show that a 4x molar excess of endophilin inhibits fission completely and decreases dynamin ' s GTPase activity . We measured fission rates and efficiencies for different endophilin - dynamin molar ratios , and concluded that the inhibition was not only a time delay but also a decrease in fission efficiency until complete blockage . Deletion construct experiments indicated that both endophilin ' s membrane binding and direct dynamin binding properties were required for full inhibition . EM images and class averaging visualised the endophilin - dynamin co - complex , where 2 to 3 turns of endophilin bind to the membrane between the dynamin rungs in the endophilin - dynamin co - complex . This explained the increased dynamin pitch that had been observed earlier on blocked elongated vesicle necks ( Iversen et al . , 2003 ; Takei et al . , 1998 ; Takei et al . , 1995 ) . Fission inhibition was found to be coupled to pitch elongation as the dynamin fluorescence intensity decreased 2‒3 fold on the endophilin - dynamin co - polymer blocked for fission , consistently with the ~ 2 fold pitch increase between the dynamin rungs observed by EM . Our results support the following model : While the adjacent dynamin rings in the helix interact , which is needed for the stimulation of GTPase activity and constriction ( Fig . 4G ) , endophilin prevents the formation of long 1 - start helices of dynamin with many inter - rung interactions between G domains in trans . Rather , when endophilin binds dynamin and the membrane of the tubule , dynamin appears unable to form the multi - turn helical coat . In the hybrid coat of the co - polymer , the BAR domains of endophilin are preventing the G - domains of adjacent dynamin dimers from interacting ( Fig . 4H ) . As both GTPase activity and GTP hydrolysis - driven constriction would therefore be inhibited , fission is blocked in the co - polymer . Interestingly , all known BAR , N - BAR and F - BAR partners of dynamin have been shown to change the architecture of the dynamin coat in similar ways when co - assembled 17 on membrane tubules ( Itoh et al . , 2005 ) . This observation and our results suggest that all BAR , N - BAR and F - BAR proteins with SH3 domains that bind the PRD domain of dynamin can potentially inhibit membrane fission by inserting of their BAR domain between the dynamin helical turns . Endophilin has previously been proposed to recruit dynamin to vesicle necks ( Shupliakov , 1997 ; Sundborger et al . , 2011 ; Wigge et al . , 1997 ) . According to our and previous findings ( Farsad et al . , 2001 ) , this endophilin - dynamin co - complex would , on the other hand , not allow for fission . Strikingly , all endocytic events blocked at the dynamin stage show a dynamin polymer with an elongated pitch . This suggests that dynamin , as it co - assembles with endophilin ( Wu et al . , 2010 ) at clathrin coated pits , is primarily assembled into an constriction - inhibited polymer . Endophilin and the other endocytic proteins could prepare the vesicle neck for fission , by decreasing the diameter of the neck and by recruiting dynamin , but fission would not be possible yet . Release of the inhibition could occur by phosphorylation of the PRD domain of dynamin upon an intracellular Ca 2 + increase , which decreases the affinity between dynamin ' s PRD and endophilin and might cause endophilin to be released from dynamin ( Chen - Hwang et al . , 2002 ) . It is unclear though whether the phosphorylation of the PRD of dynamin is possible when it is bound to endophilin ' s SH3 domain . At least when amphiphysin , another N - BAR protein , was present , the phosphorylation of dynamin ' s PRD was inhibited ( Tan et al . , 2003 ) . Also the increased Ca 2 + concentration itself is proposed to induce an intramolecular bridge within endophilin , where its SH3 domain binds to another part of the endophilin molecule causing its release from the PRD of dynamin ( Chen et al . , 2003 ) . The question remains whether the dissociation of the SH3 domain from the PRD of dynamin is enough to release endophilin from the vesicle neck . Another possibility would be the phosphorylation of the BAR domain of endophilin by LRRK2 , which was shown to reduce endophilin ' s membrane binding properties ( Matta et al . , 18 2012 ) . We speculate that this could be one reason why the kinase activity of LRRK2 is important for synaptic vesicle endocytosis ( Arranz et al . , 2015 ) . It is also still unclear whether all other BAR proteins present at the neck have to undergo the same inhibition release mechanism . 19 REFERENCES Antonny , B . , Burd , C . , De Camilli , P . , Chen , E . , Daumke , O . , Faelber , K . , Ford , M . , Frolov , V . Scale bar in magnification in magenta box , 1 µm . 4 . 3 Summary Of Article 2 71 4 . 3 Summary Of Article 2 The presented article had the aim to clarify the role of the N - BAR protein endophilin on dynamin - mediated membrane ﬁssion . Diﬀerent membrane templates and assays were used to study the eﬀect on ﬁssion . Treating tubules coated either with dynamin alone or the endophilin - dynamin co - complex with GTP indicated generally that the co - complex did not induce membrane ﬁssion . The malachite green assay indicated that dynamin had a reduced GTPase activity in the co - complex . Attaching beads to dynamin or endophilin - dynamin coated membrane tubules and monitoring the bead rotation upon GTP injection visualised that the co - complex was apparently not able to constrict . The nanotube pulling assay was used to measure ﬁssion eﬃciencies and rates for diﬀerent molecular ratios of endophilin and dynamin in the co - complex . In a condition with 4x more endophilin , ﬁssion was completely blocked , whereas dynamin alone would induce ﬁssion of all tubes within a few tens of seconds . Experiments with endophilin’s BAR or SH3 domains alone indicated that the binding between endophilin and dynamin as well as membrane binding or scaﬀolding via the BAR domain were required for complete ﬁssion inhibition . A collaboration with Nathaniel Talledge and Adam Frost from the University of California San Francisco ( UCSF ) made it possible to visualise the endophilin - dynamin co - complex on membrane tubes by electron microscopy . The previously obtained results of a dynamin pitch increase in the co - complex were conﬁrmed , but especially , the better resolution 3D averages from cryo electron microscopy showed that 2 or 3 lines of endophilin intercalated between the dynamin helix turns in the co - polymer . The 3D averages also showed that the GTPase domains of adjacent helix turns likely do not interact in the co - polymer because they are too far away . This was striking , because it allowed to make a hypothesis for the ﬁssion inhibition in the co - complex with a clear prediction : If the dynamin helix turns are further apart in the co - complex , then the dynamin ﬂuorescence signal on tubes from the nano tube pulling assay should be reduced in the co - complex . This was measured and found to be true . The reduction in dynamin signal was 2 – 3 fold . To link this information with ﬁssion , the tubes with diﬀerent endophilin - dynamin ratios and which had served for the measurements were then subjected to GTP treatment to measure ﬁssion rates , and indeed ﬁssion was blocked in 90 % of the tubes that had were covered with the co - polymer and where the dynamin signal was reduced . These results conﬁrmed the hypothesis and allowed to propose the following model : Fission is inhibited in the co - complex because endophilin inserts between the dynamin helix turns and pushes them so far apart that the GTPase domains cannot interact , hence cannot constrict , and therefore cannot mediate membrane ﬁssion . 4 . 4 Complementary Experiments 4 . 4 . 1 Injection Of Endophilin On Pre - Formed Dynamin Polymers Having added a third micromanipulator to the nanotube pulling setup , I also had the possi - bility to observe protein binding when both proteins ( dynamin and endophilin ) were injected 72 Thesis Work : Endophilin Inhibits Dynamin - Mediated Fission FIGURE 3 A B Kymograph 2 : Dynamin + endophilin on 80 : 20 tube 20141210 _ 009 5µM dynamin , 5 µM endophilin + 15µM GTP , master mix Sep 2014 ( 3 months old ) , white scale bar 5µm , black scale bar 1 min - Dynamin expansion from endophilin - dynamin copolymer possible during second injection of dynamin ( downfacing arrows ) - Dynamin signal did NOT increase upon endophilin injection ( top arrow ; no dynamin was in solution anymore when endophilin was injected ) . - Dynamin polymer length did NOT increase upon endophilin injection = > No evidence from this that endophilin is able to push apart the dynamin helix here - Aspect of some Dynamin polymers changed upon injection of endophilin ( + GTP ) , see lower upfacing arrow . - Fission took place .
